Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Conditions and Effects of Retracting Testimony
Defines retraction, its conditions, rulings, and dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid retraction of testimony, distinguish the legal consequences (daman, hadd, ta'zir), and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a witness who marries the subject of his testimony.

Core Idea
Retraction of testimony is only valid before the judge; it repents false testimony but may still incur liability or punishment.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the intricate rules governing retraction of testimony. Retraction is not merely a private act; it must occur in the judge's court to be valid. The text distinguishes between financial liability for property loss and personal punishments like hadd and ta'zir, and it records a notable intra-Hanafi dispute about a witness who marries the woman he testified about.

Guided Path
1
Define retraction and its verbal formula
Identify the required wording: 'I testified falsely' or 'I lied'. Simple denial is not retraction.
2
Identify the condition for validity
Retraction is only valid in the judge's court (majlis al-qadi). Understand the wisdom: it is a formal annulment of testimony, and testimony itself is given in court.
3
Distinguish the two aspects of the ruling
The ruling has two aspects: financial (daman) and personal (hadd/ta'zir). For daman, note the cause, conditions, and measure. For personal, distinguish between hadd (only in zina cases) and ta'zir (for other false testimony).
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
If a witness testifies to a woman's divorce, then marries her and retracts, Abu Hanifa says no annulment; Muhammad and later Abu Yusuf say annulment because the witness is believed regarding his own right.
The mufta bihi is the view of Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.
5
Understand the effect of retraction on judgment
Even if witnesses retract after judgment, the judgment stands. The parties must act on it even if they know the testimony was false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات باب الرجوع عن الشهادة يرجع بزور فيما شهدت به أو كذبت في شهادتي فلو أنكرها لم يكن رجوعاً كما في خزانة المفتين . الرابع في شرطه مجلس القاضي فلا يصح الرجوع في غيره وفائدته عدم قبول البينة على رجوعه وعدم استحلافه إذا أنكر كما سيأتي . الخامس في صفته قال في العناية : إنه أمر مشروع مرغوب فيه ديانة لأن فيه خلاصاً من عقاب الكبيرة ا هـ. وذكر الشارح أن شهادة الزور وكتمان الشهادة بالحق سواء فإذا شهد بزور عمداً أو خطأ وجبت عليه التوبة، وهي لا تصح إلا عند الحاكم ولا يمنعه عنها الاستحياء من المخلوقين وفيه تدارك ما أتلف بالزور ا هـ. السادس في حكمه : أحدهما وهو شيئان : إلى ماله والآخر إلى نفسه، فالأول الضمان ويحتاج إلى بيان ثلاثة : سببه وشرائطه ومقداره فسببه إتلاف المال أو النفس وجوب بها فإن وقعت إتلافاً انعقدت سبباً لوجوب الضمان وإلا فلا تنزيلاً للسبب منزلة المباشرة وسيأتي بيانه مفصلاً. وشرطه كونه بعد القضاء ومجلس القضاء وكون المتلف بها عيناً فلا ضمان لو رجع عن منفعة كالنكاح بعد الدخول ومنفعة دار شهدا على المؤجر للمستأجر بإجارتها بأقل من أجر مثلها ثم رجعا وأن يكون الإتلاف بغير عوض لأنه بعوض إتلاف صورة لا معنى، وقدر الواجب على قدر الإتلاف لأنه السبب والحكم يتقدر بقدر العلة. وأما ما يرجع إلى نفسه فنوعان : وجوب الحد في شهادة الزنا سواء كان قبل القضاء أو بعده للقذف منهم ولو بعد الإمضاء رجماً كان أو جلداً خلافاً لزفر في الرجم، ووجوب وهو الدية عليهم إن رجعوا بعد الرجم لا بعد الجلد وإن مات منه . والثاني وجوب التعزير عليه سوى شهادة الزنا إن تعمد الشهادة بالزور فظهر عند القاضي بإقراره؛ كذا في البدائع . فلا ضمان لو أتلفا حقاً. من الحقوق كالعفو عن القصاص لو شهدا به ثم رجعا أو الرجعة أو تسليم الشفعة أو إسقاط خيار من الخيارات؛ كذا في النتف ولا فرق في وجوب التعزير بين كونه قبل القضاء أو بعده وفي فتح القدير : ولا يخلو عن نظر لأن الرجوع ظاهر في أنه توبه عن تعمد الزور إن تعمده والتهور والعجلة إن كان أخطأ فيه ولا تعزير على التوبة ولا عن ذنب ارتفع بها وليس فيه حد مقدر ا هـ . قلت : إن رجوعه قد يكون لقصد إتلاف الحق والجواز كون المشهود عليه غره بمال لا لما ذكره ولكنه خاص بما قبل القضاء، وأما بعده فقد يظن بجهله أنه إتلاف على المشهود له أنه إتلاف لماله بالغرامة .

الضمان

قوله : (ولا يصح الرجوع إلا عند القاضي لأنه فسخ للشهادة فيختص بما يختص به الشهادة من مجلس القاضي، ولأن الرجوع توبة وهي على حسب الجناية فالسر بالسر

بعضاً كما سيذكره المؤلف وشأن المتون ،الاختصار، ولذا ترجم في التتارخانية بالكتاب وذكر تحته ستة عشر فصلاً ساقها على نسق و به اندفع ما وجه به كلام المصنف مشيراً به إلى الاعتراض على الهداية

قوله : (التعزيز) المراد بالتعزير التشهير .

٢١٦ كتاب الشهادات باب الرجوع عن الشهادة قاضي عند رجع يعزر والإعلان بالإعلان أطلقه فشمل القاضي المشهود عنده وغيره فإذا لم يصح الرجوع عند غير القاضي ولو شرطياً ـ كما في فتح القدير - وادعى المشهود عليه رجوعهما وأراد يمينهما لا يحلفان، وكذا لا تقبل بينته عليهما لأنه ادعى رجوعاً باطلاً حتى لو أقام بينة أنه كذا وضمنه المال تقبل لأن السبب صحيح، ولو أقر عند القاضي أنه رجع عند غير القاضي فإنه صحيح وإن أقر برجوع باطل لأنه يجعل إنشاء للحال. وفي خزانة المفتين : إذا رجعا عن شهادتهما وأشهدا بمال على أنفسهما لأجل الرجوع ثم جحدا ذلك فشهد عليهم الشهود بالمال من قبل الرجوع والضمان لا تقبل إذا تصادقا عند القاضي أن الإقرار بهذا السبب فالقاضي لا يلزمهما الضمان وفي المحيط : ولو ادعى رجوعهما عند القاضي ولم يدع القضاء بالرجوع والضمان لا تسمع منه البينة ولا يحلف عليه لأن الرجوع لا يصح ولا يصير موجباً للضمان إلا باتصال القضاء به كالشهادة ا هـ قوله : (فإن رجعا قبل حكمه لم يقض بها لأن الحق إنما يثبت بالقضاء والقاضي لا يقضي بكلام متناقض، وقدمنا أنه قبل الحكم أيضاً. أطلقه فشمل ما لو رجعا عن بعضها كما لو شهدا بدار وبنائها أو بأتان وولدها ثم رجعا في البناء والولد لم يقض بالأصل كما في جامع الفصولين معللاً بأن الشاهد فسق نفسه وشهادة الفاسق ترد. وفي منية المفتي : شهدا على رجل فلم يقض بشهادتهما حتى شهد رجلان عليهما أنهما رجعا عن تلك الشهادة، فإن كان اللذان أخبرا عنهما بالرجوع يعرفهما القاضي ويعدلهما وقف الأمر ولم ينفذ شهادتهما . شهد أنه سرق من هذا ثم قالا غلطنا أو وهمنا بل سرق من هذا لم يقض بها أصلاً لأنهما أقرا بالغفلة. شهد الرجل ثم زادا فيها قبل القضاء بها أو بعده وقالا أوهمنا إن كانا عدلين غير متهمين قبل ذلك منهما ا هـ . وشمل ما إذا شهذا بطلاقها ثم تزوجت فرجع أحدهما لم يفرق بينهما وبين زوجها، واختلفوا فيما إذا تزوجها أحدهما ثم رجع ففي الكافي للحاكم أن الشعبي لم يفرق بينهما وبه كان يأخذ أبو حنيفة. وقال محمد : لا يصدق على إبطال شهادته الأولى ولكنه يصدق في حق نفسه، فإن كان تزوجها فرق بينهما ورجع أبو يوسف إلى هذا القول بعد ذلك اهـ. وقد أفاد قوله «لم ينقض أن المشهود له وعليه يعملان بمقتضاه وإن علما أن الشهود زور فلو شهدا عليه بالطلاق الثلاث وقضى به ثم رجعا والزوج يعلم أنهما كاذبان لم يسعه أن يقربها؛ كذا في

قوله : (لأن الرجوع لا يصح ولا يصير موجباً للضمان إلا باتصال القضاء به) قال في الفتح: وزاد جماعة في صحة الرجوع أن يحكم القاضي برجوعهما ويضمنهما المال وإليه أشار المصنف ونقل هذا عن شيخ الإسلام، واستبعد بعض من المحققين توقف صحة الرجوع على القضاء بالرجوع أو بالضمان، وترك بعض المتأخرين من مصنفي الفتاوى هذا القيد وذكر أنه إنما تركه تعويلاً على هذا الاستبعاد قوله : (وشمل ما إذا شهدا بطلاقها إلى آخر القولة مقدم عن محله وحقه أن يكتب في آخر
Book of Testimonies, Chapter on Retraction of Testimony. Retraction occurs by stating 'I testified falsely' or 'I lied in my testimony'. If he denies it, it is not retraction, as in Khizanat al-Muftin. Fourth: its condition is the court of the judge, so retraction is invalid elsewhere, and its benefit is the non-acceptance of evidence of his retraction and he is not put on oath if he denies, as will come. Fifth: its description; al-Inayah says: It is a legitimate act, desirable religiously because it contains deliverance from the punishment of a major sin. The commentator mentioned that false testimony and concealment of true testimony are equal. So if one testifies falsely intentionally or mistakenly, repentance becomes obligatory, and it is not valid except before the judge, and modesty before creatures should not prevent him from it, and it includes rectifying what was destroyed by falsehood. Sixth: its ruling: one of two things: concerning wealth and concerning himself. The first is liability (daman), and it requires explanation of three things: its cause, conditions, and amount. Its cause is destruction of property or life by means of it; if it results in destruction, it becomes a cause for liability, otherwise not, treating the cause as direct action. Its conditions: that it be after judgment and in the court, and that the destroyed thing be a tangible asset; so no liability if retracting from a usufruct like marriage after consummation or rental of a house if they testified for the lessor against the lessee for less than fair rent and then retracted; and that the destruction be without compensation, because with compensation it is destruction in form not substance. The amount owed is proportional to the destruction, because it is the cause and the ruling is proportional to the cause. As for what relates to himself: two types: obligation of the fixed punishment (hadd) in testimony of zina, whether before or after judgment, due to the slander involved, even after execution whether stoning or flogging, contrary to Zufr regarding stoning; and obligation of blood money (diya) if they retract after stoning but not after flogging, even if the person dies from it. The second is obligation of discretionary punishment (ta'zir) on him, except for testimony of zina, if he intentionally gave false testimony and it became apparent before the judge through his confession, as stated in al-Bada'i'. So no liability if they destroy a right, such as pardoning qisas, or returning a wife, or handing over pre-emption, or dropping an option, as stated in al-Nutaf. There is no difference in the obligation of ta'zir whether before or after judgment. In Fath al-Qadir: this is not without consideration, because retraction apparently is repentance for intentional falsehood if he intended it, or haste and rashness if he erred; there is no ta'zir for repentance or for a sin removed by it, and there is no fixed measure. I say: his retraction may be for the purpose of destroying the right, and the possibility that the person testified against deceived him regarding wealth, not for what he mentioned, but it is specific to before judgment. After judgment, he might ignorantly think that it destroys the right of the person for whom he testified, that it destroys his wealth by the indemnity. Liability. His statement: (Retraction is not valid except before the judge, because it is annulment of testimony, so it is restricted to what testimony is restricted to, namely the court. And because retraction is repentance, and it is according to the offense, so secrecy with secrecy... partially as the author will mention, and the style of the texts is brevity. Hence it was translated in al-Tatarakhaniyya as a book and under it he brought sixteen sections arranged in sequence, and by it is repelled what the author's words were directed at, indicating objection to al-Hidayah. His statement: (al-Ta'zir) means ta'zir is public exposure. Page 216: Book of Testimonies, Chapter on Retraction of Testimony. A judge, when retracted, he is given ta'zir. And public exposure with public exposure. He made it general, so it includes the judge before whom testimony was given and others. So if retraction is invalid before other than the judge, even a police chief, as in Fath al-Qadir, and the person testified against claims their retraction and wants their oath, they are not sworn. Similarly, his evidence against them is not accepted, because he claims an invalid retraction. So if he brings evidence that it was so and he guarantees the money, it is accepted because the cause is valid. If he confesses before the judge that he retracted before other than the judge, it is valid, even though he confesses to an invalid retraction, because it is considered an initiation of the situation. In Khizanat al-Muftin: If they both retracted their testimony and made witnesses to wealth against themselves for the sake of retraction, then they denied that, and witnesses testified against them concerning the wealth from before retraction and liability, it is not accepted if they both affirm before the judge that the confession was for this reason; the judge does not impose liability on them. In al-Muhit: If he claims their retraction before the judge but does not claim the judgment of retraction and liability, his evidence is not heard and he is not sworn, because retraction is not valid and does not become a cause for liability unless connected to judgment, like testimony. His statement: (If they retract before his judgment, he does not judge by it because the right is only established by judgment, and the judge does not judge with contradictory speech. And we presented that before judgment as well. He made it general, so it includes if they retract from part of it, as if they testified about a house and its construction, or about a donkey and its offspring, then retracted about the construction and offspring, he does not judge the original, as in Jami' al-Fusulayn, reasoned that the witness caused himself to be immoral, and the testimony of an immoral person is rejected. In Munyat al-Mufti: They testified against a man, and he did not judge by their testimony until two men testified against them that they retracted that testimony. If he who informed about their retraction is known to the judge and deemed upright, he suspends the matter and does not execute their testimony. They testified that he stole from this person, then they said we erred or made a mistake, rather he stole from this other person, he does not judge by it at all because they admitted negligence. Two men testified, then they added to it before or after judgment and said 'we made a mistake', if they are upright and not accused, it is accepted from them. It includes the case where they testified to her divorce, then she married, and one of them retracted; he does not separate them from her husband. They differed concerning the case where one of them married her and then retracted. In al-Kafi for al-Hakim: al-Sha'bi did not separate them, and Abu Hanifa used to take this view. Muhammad said: He is not believed to invalidate his first testimony, but he is believed regarding his own right. If he married her, they are separated; and Abu Yusuf later returned to this view. His statement 'not overturned' indicates that the person for whom and against whom testimony is given act according to it even if they know the witnesses are false. So if they testified against him for triple divorce and the judge judged by it, then they retracted, and the husband knows they are liars, it is not permissible for him to approach her. His statement: (Because retraction is not valid and does not become a cause for liability unless connected to judgment) said in al-Fath: And a group added to the validity of retraction that the judge judge their retraction and impose liability on them for the money, and the author indicated this, and this is transmitted from Shaykh al-Islam. Some of the verifiers considered the stoppage of the validity of retraction on judgment of retraction or liability as improbable. Some later compilers of fatwas omitted this condition, stating that they omitted it relying on this improbability. His statement: (And it includes the case where they testified to her divorce... to the end of the statement) is advanced from its place, and it should be written at the end.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the chapter of retraction of testimony. It opens by defining the verbal formula of retraction: the witness must say 'I testified falsely' or 'I lied'. Simple denial of having testified is not retraction. The commentator then lists several aspects: the condition (that it must be in the judge's court), the description (it is a recommended religious act as it is repentance from a major sin), and the ruling, which is divided into two: matters concerning wealth (liability) and matters concerning the person (fixed punishment or discretionary punishment). The explanation of liability covers its cause (destruction of property by the testimony), conditions (must be after judgment, in court, the destroyed item must be a tangible asset, and destruction must be without compensation), and measure (proportional to the destruction). For personal matters: fixed punishment (hadd) applies only in zina testimony due to slander; blood money (diya) applies if retraction occurs after stoning; and discretionary punishment (ta'zir) applies for intentional false testimony otherwise. The commentary also discusses a nuanced point: retraction may be considered repentance, but if done with intent to harm, it may still incur ta'zir. The text then delves into the requirement that retraction must be before the judge, and the consequences of retracting before or after judgment, including partial retraction and its effect on the remaining testimony. An intra-Hanafi dispute is recorded: if a witness testifies to a woman's divorce, then marries her and retracts, Abu Hanifa (following al-Sha'bi) holds that the couple is not separated, while Muhammad and later Abu Yusuf say they are separated because he is believed regarding his own right. The passage concludes by emphasizing that even if the parties know the witnesses are false, they must act on the judgment; the husband cannot approach his wife after a judgment of triple divorce based on false testimony if the witnesses later retract but the husband knows they lied.

Key Terms
الرجوع (al-ruju'): Legal retraction of testimony by stating 'I testified falsely' or 'I lied'; must be done before the judge.
الضمان (al-daman): Financial liability imposed on witnesses who retract after their testimony caused destruction of property, provided conditions are met.
التعزير (al-ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for false testimony when the fixed punishment (hadd) does not apply; defined here as public exposure.
التوبة (al-tawbah): Repentance from false testimony, which is obligatory; retraction before the judge is its form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in the passage, when is the retraction of testimony valid?
A) At any time and place
B) Only before the judge who heard the case
C) Before any public official
D) Only after judgment has been executed

Key Takeaway
Retraction of testimony is a formal act before the judge; it serves as repentance but does not automatically erase legal consequences like liability or discretionary punishment.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
General Ruling: Retraction Before Judgment Voids Testimony
Ruling with proof and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that retraction before judgment voids the entire testimony, and explain the reasoning (tafsiq) and its application to partial retraction.

Core Idea
Retraction before judgment makes the witness a fasiq, voiding the entire testimony, including parts not retracted.

In this lesson, we delve into the foundational principle of retraction of testimony before the judge's verdict. The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains why a witness's contradictory statements discredit him, leading to the rejection of his testimony. We will also see how this applies when witnesses retract only part of their testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Find the core ruling: If witnesses retract before judgment, their testimony is not implemented. The text states: 'فإن رجعا قبل حكمه لم يقض بها'.
2
Understand the proof (talil)
The reasoning is that the right is only established by judgment, and the judge cannot act on contradictory speech. Also, the witness discredits himself (tafsiq).
3
Apply to partial retraction
The text gives the example of testifying about a house and its building, then retracting only the building. The entire testimony is void because the witness becomes a fasiq.
The witness has disqualified himself.
4
Explore additional examples
Other scenarios: witnesses who say 'we erred' (admitted negligence) are not accepted; witnesses who add testimony due to forgetfulness are accepted if upright.

كتاب الشهادات باب الرجوع عن الشهادة قاضي عند رجع يعزر والإعلان بالإعلان أطلقه فشمل القاضي المشهود عنده وغيره فإذا لم يصح الرجوع عند غير القاضي ولو شرطياً ـ كما في فتح القدير - وادعى المشهود عليه رجوعهما وأراد يمينهما لا يحلفان، وكذا لا تقبل بينته عليهما لأنه ادعى رجوعاً باطلاً حتى لو أقام بينة أنه كذا وضمنه المال تقبل لأن السبب صحيح، ولو أقر عند القاضي أنه رجع عند غير القاضي فإنه صحيح وإن أقر برجوع باطل لأنه يجعل إنشاء للحال. وفي خزانة المفتين : إذا رجعا عن شهادتهما وأشهدا بمال على أنفسهما لأجل الرجوع ثم جحدا ذلك فشهد عليهم الشهود بالمال من قبل الرجوع والضمان لا تقبل إذا تصادقا عند القاضي أن الإقرار بهذا السبب فالقاضي لا يلزمهما الضمان وفي المحيط : ولو ادعى رجوعهما عند القاضي ولم يدع القضاء بالرجوع والضمان لا تسمع منه البينة ولا يحلف عليه لأن الرجوع لا يصح ولا يصير موجباً للضمان إلا باتصال القضاء به كالشهادة ا هـ . قوله : (فإن رجعا قبل حكمه لم يقض بها لأن الحق إنما يثبت بالقضاء والقاضي لا يقضي بكلام متناقض، وقدمنا أنه قبل الحكم أيضاً. أطلقه فشمل ما لو رجعا عن بعضها كما لو شهدا بدار وبنائها أو بأتان وولدها ثم رجعا في البناء والولد لم يقض بالأصل كما في جامع الفصولين معللاً بأن الشاهد فسق نفسه وشهادة الفاسق ترد. وفي منية المفتي : شهدا على رجل فلم يقض بشهادتهما حتى شهد رجلان عليهما أنهما رجعا عن تلك الشهادة، فإن كان اللذان أخبرا عنهما بالرجوع يعرفهما القاضي ويعدلهما وقف الأمر ولم ينفذ شهادتهما . شهد أنه سرق من هذا ثم قالا غلطنا أو وهمنا بل سرق من هذا لم يقض بها أصلاً لأنهما أقرا بالغفلة. شهد الرجل ثم زادا فيها قبل القضاء بها أو بعده وقالا أوهمنا إن كانا عدلين غير متهمين قبل ذلك منهما ا هـ . وشمل ما إذا شهذا بطلاقها ثم تزوجت فرجع أحدهما لم يفرق بينهما وبين زوجها، واختلفوا فيما إذا تزوجها أحدهما ثم رجع ففي الكافي للحاكم أن الشعبي لم يفرق بينهما وبه كان يأخذ أبو حنيفة. وقال محمد : لا يصدق على إبطال شهادته الأولى ولكنه يصدق في حق نفسه، فإن كان تزوجها فرق بينهما ورجع أبو يوسف إلى هذا القول بعد ذلك اهـ.
Book of Testimonies, Chapter of Retraction of Testimony. A judge, when retraction occurs, he disciplines and publicizes. He [the author] gave it absolutely, so it includes the judge before whom testimony was given and others. So if retraction is not valid before a non-judge, even if conditional — as in Fath al-Qadir — and the defendant claims their retraction and wants their oath, they are not sworn. Similarly, his evidence against them is not accepted because he claimed a false retraction. Even if he brings evidence that it was so and he guaranteed the property, it is accepted because the cause is sound. And if he acknowledges before the judge that he retracted before a non-judge, it is valid, even if he acknowledges a false retraction, because it is treated as an initiation of the situation. In Khizanat al-Muftin: If they retract their testimony and have witnesses to a property against themselves for the sake of retraction, then deny that, so witnesses testify against them for the property due to the retraction and guarantee, it is not accepted if they both agree before the judge that the acknowledgment was for this reason; the judge does not impose the guarantee on them. In al-Muhit: And if he claims their retraction before the judge and does not claim the judgment of retraction and guarantee, evidence from him is not heard and an oath is not imposed on him because retraction is not valid and does not become a cause for guarantee except by attachment to the judgment, like testimony. End quote. His statement: (If they retract before his judgment, it is not implemented because the right is only established by judgment, and the judge does not rule with contradictory speech. And we have stated that it is before the judgment as well. He gave it absolutely, so it includes if they retract part of it, as if they testified about a house and its building, or a female donkey and its offspring, then they retracted regarding the building and offspring, the original is not implemented, as in Jami' al-Fusulain, reasoned that the witness has disqualified himself and the testimony of a corrupt person is rejected. In Munyat al-Mufti: Two witness testified against a man, and their testimony was not implemented until two men testified against them that they retracted that testimony. If the two who informed about their retraction are known by the judge and are reliable, he suspends the matter and does not enforce their testimony. If they testified that he stole from this person, then they said, 'We erred or we made a mistake, rather he stole from this person,' it is not implemented at all because they admitted to negligence. If a man testified, then they added to it before implementation or after, and said, 'We forgot,' if they are upright and not suspect, it is accepted from them. End quote. And it includes if they testified to his divorce, then she married, then one of them retracted, the couple is not separated. They disagreed about if one of them married her then retracted. In al-Kafi of al-Hakim, al-Sha'bi did not separate them, and Abu Hanifa used to take that. Muhammad said: He is not believed to invalidate his first testimony, but he is believed regarding his own self. So if he married her, they are separated between them. And Abu Yusuf later retracted to this view. End quote.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with commentary. It begins by discussing the general principle that retraction of testimony is only valid if made before the judge who heard the case. Retraction before a non-judge is not valid, as it cannot lead to liability without being attached to a judicial proceeding. The author then quotes the matn: 'If they retract before his judgment, it is not implemented.' The reason is that the right is only established by judgment, and a judge cannot act on contradictory speech. The commentary expands to include partial retraction: if witnesses testify to both a principal and its accessory (e.g., a house and its building), then retract only the accessory, the entire testimony is void because the witness has disqualified himself by admitting inconsistency, and the testimony of a fasiq (corrupt person) is rejected. Several examples from Munyat al-Mufti illustrate this: if other witnesses testify that the original witnesses retracted and the judge knows them to be reliable, he suspends the matter; if witnesses say 'we erred' about the identity of the thief, it is not accepted because they admit negligence; if witnesses add to their testimony before or after judgment and attribute it to forgetfulness, it is accepted if they are upright. An intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned: if witnesses testified to a divorce, then the woman remarried, then one witness retracted, the couple is not separated. However, if the witness himself married her and then retracted, Imam Muhammad held that he is believed regarding himself (so the marriage is invalid), and Abu Yusuf later adopted this view. The commentary ends here.

Key Terms
الرجوع (al-ruju'): The act of a witness withdrawing his testimony before or after judgment.
الشهادة (al-shahadah): Testimony given in court to establish a right.
القضاء (al-qada'): The judge's verdict based on testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If witnesses testify about a house and its building, then retract only about the building, what is the ruling?
A) The testimony about the house remains valid, the building part is void
B) The entire testimony about both is void
C) Only the building part is void, the house is unaffected
D) The judge may choose which part to accept

Key Takeaway
A witness's retraction before judgment voids the entire testimony because it discredits his honesty.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: A Witness Who Marries the Woman
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of a witness's retraction on his own marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on whether a witness's retraction is accepted when he himself marries the woman, and state the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
A witness who marries the woman is believed regarding himself, voiding the marriage if he retracts.

This passage presents a specific intra-Hanafi disagreement: if a witness testifies to a divorce, then later marries the woman and retracts his testimony, does his retraction affect the marriage? Abu Hanifa and al-Sha'bi held that it does not, while Muhammad (and later Abu Yusuf) held that the witness is believed about himself, so the marriage is invalid. We will explore the reasoning and the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Witnesses testify that a woman is divorced. She then marries. One of the witnesses retracts. Later, that witness himself marries the woman.
2
Identify the disagreement
Abu Hanifa (and al-Sha'bi) say the retraction does not affect the marriage of the other witness? Actually the scenario is: one witness retracts after the woman marries someone else, then that witness himself marries her. The ikhtilaf is about whether his retraction is accepted to invalidate his own marriage.
3
Explain Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa: The witness is not believed to invalidate his first testimony, so the marriage based on that testimony stands (i.e., he is not separated from her).
Followed al-Sha'bi's practice.
4
Explain Muhammad's view
Muhammad: The witness is not believed to invalidate his testimony regarding others, but he is believed regarding himself. So if he married her, he is believed that his earlier testimony was false, and the marriage is void.
5
State the mufta bihi
Abu Yusuf later adopted Muhammad's view, making it the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Shahadat — Testimony

Retraction of Testimony After Judgment: Final Hanafi Position
Intra-Hanafi dispute on retraction effect and liability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the final Hanafi ruling on retraction of testimony after judgment and explain the liability of witnesses using the analogy of the well-digger.

Core Idea
Retraction after judgment never overturns the verdict; witnesses must compensate the defendant if property was taken.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a critical issue in Hanafi testimony law: what happens when witnesses retract their testimony after the judge has already issued a verdict? The general rule is clear – the verdict stands – but there was an early intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the retraction could overturn the judgment if the witness is more reliable at the time of retraction. The author critically refines this position, rejecting the detailed view and affirming the final school stance: the verdict is never overturned, and the witnesses become liable for compensation if the plaintiff has taken property based on their testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Main Ruling from the Matn
The matn phrase 'is not overturned' indicates the core rule: retraction after judgment does not nullify the verdict. The commentator explains that the first statement (testimony) is given weight because the judgment is attached to it, and the later contradictory statement cannot undo it.
This applies regardless of the witness's reliability at the time of retraction.
2
Understand the Refutation of the Detailed View
A view attributed to al-Muhit suggested that if the witness is more reliable at retraction, the judgment is overturned. The author refutes this by citing numerous sources (Fath al-Qadir, al-Kafi, al-Bazzaziyya) showing that Abu Hanifa himself retracted this early opinion, and the school settled on the position that the verdict stands in all cases.
The author personally checked al-Muhit al-Sarakhsi and found agreement with the majority without such detail.
3
Examine the Basis for Liability
The witnesses are liable because they indirectly caused the plaintiff's loss. The judge, as the direct cause, is compelled to rule and is exempt from liability. This is analogized to the digger of a well (qiyas): just as a person who digs a well on public property is liable for anyone who falls in, the witnesses are liable for the loss they tortiously caused.
Ta'zir (discretionary punishment) is also imposed on the witnesses for retracting.
4
Distinguish Between Retraction and Other Defects
The rule that the verdict stands is specific to retraction. If it becomes apparent that the witness was a slave or a convicted slanderer (qadhf), the judgment is annulled. This is because such defects go to the qualifications of the witness, whereas retraction is a change of statement that contradicts without proving initial deficiency.
The commentator clarifies this distinction early in the passage.
5
Apply the Final Ruling
The practical consequence: if witnesses retract after judgment and the plaintiff has taken property, the judgment remains enforceable, but the witnesses become liable to compensate the defendant. The school's final position is that of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), which Abu Hanifa later adopted.
This is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) for fatwa.

وقد أفاد قوله «لم ينقض أن المشهود له وعليه يعملان بمقتضاه وإن علما أن الشهود زور فلو شهدا عليه بالطلاق الثلاث وقضى به ثم رجعا والزوج يعلم أنهما كاذبان لم يسعه أن يقربها؛ كذا في الكافي للحاكم . وقيد بالرجوع لأنه لو ظهر أن الشاهد عبد أو محدود في قذف يبطل القضاء المال إلى المقضى له ؛ كذا في كافي الحاكم . قوله : (وبعده لا ينقض) أي إن رجعا بعد الحكم لم ينقض القضاء لأن آخر كلامهم يناقض أوله فلا ينقض الحكم بالتناقض، ولأنه في الدلالة على الصدق مثل الأول وقد ترجح الأول باتصال القضاء به أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الشاهد وقت الرجوع مثل ما شهد في العدالة أو دونه أو أفضل وهكذا لم يقيد في أكثر الكتب متوناً وشروحاً وفتاوى. وفي خزانة المفتين معزياً إلى المحيط : إن كان الرجوع بعد القضاء ينظر إلى حال الراجع، فإن كان حاله عند الرجوع أفضل من حاله وقت الشهادة في العدالة صح رجوعه في حق نفسه وفي حق غيره حتى وجب عليه التعزير وينقض القضاء ويرد المال على المشهود عليه، وإن كان حاله عند الرجوع مثل حاله عند الشهادة في العدالة أو دونه وجب عليه التعزير ولا ينقض القضاء ، ولا يرد المشهود به على المشهود عليه ولا يجب الضمان على الشاهد ا هـ. وهو غير صحيح عن أهل المذهب لمخالفته ما نقلوه من وجوب الضمان على الشاهد إذا رجع الحكم، وفي هذا التفصيل عدم تضمينه مطلقاً . نقله مناقض لأنه قال أول الباب أنه في مع بالضمان موافقاً للمذهب . ثم كشفت المحيط للإمام رضي الدين السرخسي الموجود في ديارنا فوجدته وافق الجماعة من غير تفصيل فهو وإن احتمل أن يكون في المحيط البرهاني لكن يصح عن المذهب فإنهم نقلوا عدم الضمان عن الشافعي. ثم رأيت بعد ذلك في فتح القدير أن هذا قول أبي حنيفة الأول وهو قول شيخه حماد ثم رجع عنه إلى أنه لا ينقض القضاء ولا يرد المال على المقضى عليه على كل حال، ثم رأيته في الكافي للحاكم الشهيد قوله : (وضمنا ما أتلفاه للمشهود عليه إذا قبض المدعي المال لأن التسبب على وجه التعدي الضمان كحافر البئر وقد وجد سبب الإتلاف تعدياً وقد تعذر إيجاب الضمان على سبب المباشر وهو القاضي لأنه كالملجأ إلى القضاء، وفي إيجابه صرف الناس عن تقلده وتعذر استيفاؤه من المدعي لأن الحكم ماض فاعتبر التسبب. وفي المحيط : رجع الشاهدان في المرض وعليهما دين الصحة وماتا بدئ بدين الصحة لأن ما وجب عليهما بالرجوع في المرض دين المريض لأنه وجب بإقرارهما في المرض ا هـ . وإنما قيد بالقبض لأن الإتلاف به القول به لا المقولة الآتية وقد رأيته في بعض النسخ كذلك قوله : (ثم رأيت بعد ذلك في فتح القدير الخ) وهكذا قال في البزازية ثم رجع إلى قولهما وعليه استقر المذهب اهـ ومثله في التتارخانية برمز المحيط فإنه نقل عنه أن أبا حنيفة كان يقول كذا وساق التفصيل ثم قال : ثم رجع عن هذا القول وقال : لا رجوعه في حق غيره على كل حال وهو قولهما والظاهر أن المراد به المحيط البرهاني لما ذكر المؤلف أن ما في المحيط السرخسي ليس فيه التفصيل .
And his statement 'is not overturned' benefits that the one in whose favor and against whom the judgment is given act according to its requirement even if they know the witnesses were false. For example, if they testified against him with triple divorce and judgment was given, then they retracted, and the husband knows they are liars, it is not permissible for him to approach her; similarly in al-Kafi of al-Hakim. And it is restricted to retraction because if it becomes apparent that the witness was a slave or one who had been punished for qadhf, the judgment regarding the property to the successful party is annulled; similarly in al-Kafi of al-Hakim. His statement: (And after it is not overturned) meaning if they retract after the judgment, the judgment is not overturned because their last statement contradicts the first, so the judgment is not overturned by contradiction, and because it is equal to the first in indicating truth, and the first is preponderant due to the judgment being attached to it. He gave it absolutely, so it includes if the witness at the time of retraction is like his state at testimony in reliability or less or better, and thus it is not restricted in most books of texts, commentaries, and fatwas. In Khizanat al-Muftin, attributed to al-Muhit: If the retraction occurs after judgment, the state of the retractor is considered. If his state at retraction is better than his state at testimony in reliability, his retraction is valid regarding himself and others, so he must be disciplined, the judgment is overturned, and property is returned to the defendant. If his state at retraction is like his state at testimony in reliability or less, he must be disciplined, the judgment is not overturned, the property is not returned to the defendant, and the witness is not liable. End quote. This is not correct from the people of the school because it contradicts what they have transmitted of the obligation of guarantee on the witness when the judgment is retracted, and in this detail there is no guarantee at all. The transmitter is contradictory because he said at the beginning of the chapter that it is with guarantee, agreeing with the school. Then I examined the Muhit of Imam Radhi al-Din al-Sarakhsi found in our lands and found that he agreed with the majority without detail. So even if it is possible that it is in al-Muhit al-Burhani, it is not correct from the school, for they transmitted the absence of guarantee from al-Shafi'i. Then after that I saw in Fath al-Qadir that this is the first statement of Abu Hanifa and the statement of his teacher Hammad, then he retracted from it to the position that the judgment is not overturned and the property is not returned to the defeated party in any case. Then I saw in al-Kafi of al-Hakim al-Shahid his statement: (And they are liable for what they destroyed for the defendant if the plaintiff took the property, because causing destruction in a tortious manner leads to liability, like the digger of a well. And the cause of destruction has occurred tortiously, and enforcing liability on the direct cause, which is the judge, is difficult because he is compelled to judge, and enforcing it would deter people from undertaking it, and it is difficult to recover from the plaintiff because the judgment is final, so the indirect cause is considered. In al-Muhit: The two witnesses retracted in sickness while they had a debt of health and they died; the debt of health is given priority because that which became obligatory on them due to retraction in sickness is a debt of sickness because it became obligatory by their acknowledgment in sickness. End quote. And it is restricted by 'taking possession' because destruction is by it; this is the statement adopted, not the following statement. And I have seen it in some copies like that. His statement: (Then I saw after that in Fath al-Qadir [etc.]) And thus it is said in al-Bazzaziyya: then he returned to the statement of them both (the Sahibayn) and upon it the school settled. End quote. And similar in al-Tatarkhaniyya with the symbol of al-Muhit, for he transmitted that Abu Hanifa used to say thus and mentioned the detail, then said: then he retracted from this statement and said: no retraction regarding others in any case, and this is the statement of them both. And it appears that what is meant is al-Muhit al-Burhani because the author mentioned that what is in al-Muhit al-Sarakhsi does not contain the detail.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute with critical refinement. It begins by stating the general principle derived from the matn phrase 'is not overturned': the verdict remains effective even if both parties know the witnesses were false. An example: if witnesses testify to triple divorce, judgment is given, then they retract and the husband knows they lied, he cannot remarry his wife. This rule is specific to retraction; if it becomes apparent that the witness was a slave or a convicted slanderer, the judgment is annulled. The author then directly quotes the matn 'after it is not overturned' and explains the reasoning: the last statement contradicts the first, and the first is strengthened by the judge's ruling. This applies regardless of the witness's level of reliability at retraction. The author then critiques a view attributed to al-Muhit that distinguishes based on the witness's state at retraction, claiming that if he is more reliable, retraction overturns the verdict. The author asserts this is incorrect because it contradicts the established school position that the witness is always liable after retraction (if the plaintiff took property). He checks al-Muhit of al-Sarakhsi and finds it agrees with the majority without such detail. The final position, confirmed from Fath al-Qadir and al-Kafi, is that Abu Hanifa initially held the detailed view but then retracted to the position that the verdict is not overturned and the witness is liable for compensation if the plaintiff took the property. This is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi), also the view of the Sahibayn. The analogy is given: the witnesses are like a well-digger causing destruction indirectly, and since direct cause (the judge) is exempt, the indirect cause bears liability. A separate ruling: if witnesses retract during illness when they already had a debt of health, and then die, the debt of health is paid first because the obligation from retraction in illness is a debt of sickness. The passage ends by confirming that the school's final position is that retraction after judgment does not overturn the verdict but creates liability for compensation.

Key Terms
الضمان (al-daman): Liability for compensation; in this context, witnesses must compensate the defendant if the plaintiff took property based on their testimony.
التعزير (al-ta'zir): Discretionary punishment imposed by the judge for wrongdoing; here, witnesses who retract are disciplined.
التسبب (al-tasabbub): Indirect causation; the witnesses are the indirect cause of harm, as opposed to the direct cause (the judge).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If witnesses retract after judgment and the plaintiff has already taken the property, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The verdict is overturned, and the property is returned to the defendant
B) The verdict stands, but the witnesses must compensate the defendant
C) The verdict is overturned only if the witnesses are more reliable at retraction
D) The witnesses are not liable, but the judge returns the property

Key Takeaway
Retraction after judgment does not nullify the verdict, but the witnesses become liable for compensation if the plaintiff took property, based on the principle of indirect causation (tasabbub).

Shahadat — Testimony

Retraction of Testimony After Judgment: Liability and the Hanafi Dispute
Commentary expanding on retraction after judgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds witnesses liable after retraction and distinguish between the earlier and later positions regarding the condition of possession.

Core Idea
Retraction after judgment does not overturn it, but witnesses become liable for the loss caused.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines what happens when witnesses retract their testimony after the judge has already issued a verdict. While the judgment stands, the key question is whether the witnesses must compensate the losing party. The Hanafi school has a nuanced dispute, with the mufta bihi being unconditional liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the question is whether retraction after judgment overturns the verdict and/or imposes liability on the witnesses. Note that the judgment stands per Hanafi consensus.
The base rule: 'after judgment, retraction does not overturn'.
2
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute on liability
Abu Hanifa first held that if the witness at retraction is equal or less reliable, no liability. He later retracted to unconditional liability, agreeing with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Identify the first opinion and the final mufta bihi.
The earlier view is reported from Hammad; the later view is the relied-upon position.
3
Analyze the condition of possession (qabd)
Some authorities required the winner to have taken possession for liability to arise. The later position abandons this condition. Understand the reasoning: possession actualizes the loss, but judgment itself creates a right.
Al-Khulasa and others state fatwa is on unconditional liability.
4
Distinguish between 'ayn and dayn
For testimony about a specific item ('ayn), liability arises even without possession because it's a loss of a specific thing. For a debt (dayn), liability only after receipt to maintain equivalence.
This distinction appears in al-Muhit and is the view of Shaykh al-Islam.
5
Apply to dhimmi witnesses
Consider testimony about wine or a pig from dhimmis. Abu Yusuf: liable for pig value, not wine. Muhammad: liable for both. Understand the basis: what has value for dhimmis.
The passage ends with this intra-Hanafi difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات باب الرجوع عن الشهادة
ينقض وضمنا ما أتلفاه للمشهود عليه إذا قبض المدعي المال فإن رجع أحدهما ضمن الكافي للحاكم . وقيد بالرجوع لأنه لو ظهر أن الشاهد عبد أو محدود في قذف يبطل القضاء إلى المقضى له ؛ كذا في كافي الحاكم .
ويرد بعد قوله : (وبعده لا ينقض) أي إن رجعا بعد الحكم لم ينقض القضاء لأن آخر كلامهم يناقض أوله فلا ينقض الحكم بالتناقض، ولأنه في الدلالة على الصدق مثل الأول وقد ترجح الأول باتصال القضاء به أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الشاهد وقت الرجوع مثل ما شهد في العدالة أو دونه أو أفضل وهكذا لم يقيد في أكثر الكتب متوناً وشروحاً وفتاوى. وفي خزانة المفتين معزياً إلى المحيط : إن كان الرجوع بعد القضاء ينظر إلى حال الراجع، فإن كان حاله عند الرجوع أفضل من حاله وقت الشهادة في العدالة صح رجوعه في حق نفسه وفي حق غيره حتى وجب عليه التعزير وينقض القضاء ويرد المال على المشهود عليه، وإن كان حاله عند الرجوع مثل حاله عند الشهادة في العدالة أو دونه وجب عليه التعزير ولا ينقض القضاء ، ولا يرد المشهود به على المشهود عليه ولا يجب الضمان على الشاهد ا هـ. وهو غير صحيح عن أهل المذهب لمخالفته ما نقلوه من وجوب الضمان على الشاهد إذا رجع الحكم، وفي هذا التفصيل عدم تضمينه مطلقاً . نقله مناقض لأنه قال أول الباب أنه في مع بالضمان موافقاً للمذهب . ثم كشفت المحيط للإمام رضي الدين السرخسي الموجود في ديارنا فوجدته وافق الجماعة من غير تفصيل فهو وإن احتمل أن يكون في المحيط البرهاني لكن يصح عن المذهب فإنهم نقلوا عدم الضمان عن الشافعي. ثم رأيت بعد ذلك في فتح القدير أن هذا قول أبي حنيفة الأول وهو قول شيخه حماد ثم رجع عنه إلى أنه لا ينقض القضاء ولا يرد المال على المقضى عليه على كل حال، ثم رأيته في الكافي للحاكم الشهيد قوله : (وضمنا ما أتلفاه للمشهود عليه إذا قبض المدعي المال لأن التسبب على وجه التعدي الضمان كحافر البئر وقد وجد سبب الإتلاف تعدياً وقد تعذر إيجاب الضمان على سبب المباشر وهو القاضي لأنه كالملجأ إلى القضاء، وفي إيجابه صرف الناس عن تقلده وتعذر استيفاؤه من المدعي لأن الحكم ماض فاعتبر التسبب. وفي المحيط : رجع الشاهدان في المرض وعليهما دين الصحة وماتا بدئ بدين الصحة لأن ما وجب عليهما بالرجوع في المرض دين المريض لأنه وجب بإقرارهما في المرض ا هـ . وإنما قيد بالقبض لأن الإتلاف به يتحقق ولأنه لا مماثلة بين أخذ العين وإلزام الدين وقد تبع المصنف صاحب الهداية في تقييده تبعاً للإمام السرخسي وصاحب المجمع وأصحاب الفتاوى في إطلاقهم، فقد صرح في الخلاصة والبزازية وخزانة المفتين بالضمان بعد القضاء قبض المدعي بالمال أو لا قالوا: وعليه الفتوى. وفي الخلاصة إنه قول أبي حنيفة الآخر وهو قولهما ا هـ. وظاهره أنه اشتراط القبض مرجوع عنه. وفرق في المحيط بين العين والدين فقال : شهدا بعين ثم رجعا ضمناً قيمتها قبضها المشهود له أم لا، لأن ضمان الرجوع ضمان إتلاف وضمان الإتلاف مقدر بالمثل إن كان المشهود به مثلياً، وبالقيمة إن لم يكن مثلياً. وإن كان المشهود به ديناً فرجع الشهود قبل قبضه لا يضمنون، وإن قبضه المشهود له ثم رجعا ضمناً لأنهما أوجبا عليه ديناً فيجب في ذمتهما مثل ذلك، ولا يستوفى منهما إلا بعد قبض المشهود به تحقيقاً للمعادلة ا هـ. وهذا قول شيخ الإسلام وشمل أيضاً قوله ما أتلفاه خمر الذمي وخنزيره لكن في كافي الحاكم : وإذا شهد الذميان لذمي بمال أو خمر أو خنزير فقضى القاضي بذلك ثم رجعا ضمناً المال وقيمة الخنزير ولا يضمنان الخمر ولا قيمته في قول أبي يوسف، ويضمنان قيمة الخمر في قول محمد، ولو لم يسلم الشاهدان وأسلم المشهود عليه ثم رجعا عن الشهادة ضمنا قيمة الخنزير ولم يضمنا قيمة الخمر ا هـ .
Chapter of Testimonies: Section on Retraction of Testimony. ... [It is not overturned] and they are liable for what they caused loss to the person against whom the testimony was given if the claimant has taken possession of the property, [according to] al-Kafi al-Hakim. And it is restricted to retraction because if it appears that the witness is a slave or one who received hadd for slander, the judgment is invalidated to the one adjudged in his favor; likewise in Kafi al-Hakim. And it is rebutted after his statement: (And after it, it is not overturned) i.e., if they retract after the judgment, the judgment is not overturned because their last statement contradicts their first, so the judgment is not overturned due to contradiction, and because it is similar to the first in indicating truth, and the first has been given precedence by the connection of judgment to it. He made it general so it includes when the witness at the time of retraction is like his state at testimony in reliability or lower or better, and thus it was not restricted in most books of texts, commentaries, and fatwas. And in Khizanat al-Muftin, attributed to al-Muhit: If the retraction is after judgment, the state of the retractor is considered: if his state at retraction is better than his state at testimony in reliability, his retraction is valid in his own right and in the right of others, so ta'zir becomes obligatory on him, the judgment is overturned, and the property is returned to the one against whom testimony was given; and if his state at retraction is like his state at testimony in reliability or lower, ta'zir becomes obligatory on him but the judgment is not overturned, nor is the adjudged property returned to the one against whom testimony was given, nor is the witness liable. End quote. It is not correct from the people of the school because it contradicts what they transmitted of the obligation of liability on the witness when he retracts after the judgment, and in this detail there is absolute non-liability. It is contradictory because he said at the beginning of the chapter that it is... with liability in agreement with the school. Then I checked al-Muhit by Imam Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi present in our lands and found it agreed with the group without detail; so even if it is possible that it is in al-Muhit al-Burhani, it is not correct regarding the school because they transmitted non-liability from al-Shafi'i. Then I saw after that in Fath al-Qadir that this is the first opinion of Abu Hanifa, which is the opinion of his teacher Hammad, then he retracted from it to the opinion that the judgment is not overturned nor is the property returned to the one against whom judgment is given in any case. Then I saw it in al-Kafi al-Hakim al-Shahid: his statement: (And they are liable for what they caused loss to the person against whom testimony was given if the claimant has taken possession of the property) because causing loss by way of transgression necessitates liability, like the digger of a well, and the cause of loss has occurred transgressionally, and it is impossible to impose liability on the direct cause, i.e., the judge because he is compelled to judgment, and imposing it would turn people away from undertaking it, and it is impossible to exact it from the claimant because the judgment is valid, so the indirect causation is considered. And in al-Muhit: Two witnesses retracted during illness and they had debts of health and they died; they start with the debt of health because what became obligatory upon them by retraction during illness is a debt of illness because it became obligatory by their admission during illness. End quote. And he only restricted it with possession because the loss is realized by it, and because there is no correspondence between taking a specific item and imposing a debt. And the author followed the author of al-Hidayah in his restriction, following Imam al-Sarakhsi and the author of al-Majma' and the authors of fatwas in their absolute statements. For it is stated in al-Khulasa, al-Bazzaziyya, and Khizanat al-Muftin: liability after judgment whether the claimant has taken possession of the property or not; they said: and upon it is the fatwa. And in al-Khulasa it is the second opinion of Abu Hanifa and it is the opinion of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). End quote. And its apparent meaning is that the condition of possession is retracted from. And al-Muhit distinguished between a specific item and a debt: if they testified about a specific item then retracted, they are liable for its value whether the beneficiary took possession or not, because the liability of retraction is liability for loss and liability for loss is estimated by the like if the adjudged item is of a standardizable type, and by value if it is not of that type. And if the adjudged item is a debt and the witnesses retract before its receipt, they are not liable; if the beneficiary receives it then they retract, they are liable because they imposed a debt on him, so the like of that is obligatory in their liability, and it is not exacted from them except after receipt of the adjudged property to achieve equivalence. End quote. And this is the opinion of Shaykh al-Islam. And it also includes his statement: what they caused loss of: the wine and pig of a dhimmi. But in Kafi al-Hakim: If two dhimmis testify for a dhimmi regarding property, wine, or a pig, and the judge adjudicates accordingly, then they retract, they are liable for the property and the value of the pig, and they are not liable for the wine nor its value according to Abu Yusuf; they are liable for the value of the wine according to Muhammad. And if the two witnesses had not converted to Islam but the person against whom testimony was given had converted, then they retract, they are liable for the value of the pig and they are not liable for the value of the wine. End quote.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the consequences when witnesses retract their testimony after a judgment has been passed. The author begins by stating the rule from al-Kafi al-Hakim: if witnesses retract after judgment, the judgment is not overturned, but they are jointly liable for the loss caused to the losing party if the winner has taken possession of the property. This liability is based on the principle that the witnesses caused loss through transgression, similar to digging a well. The commentary then examines a detail reported from Khizanat al-Muftin, which attempts to differentiate based on the witness's level of reliability at retraction compared to the time of testimony. This detail suggests that if the witness is more reliable at retraction, the judgment is overturned; if not, the judgment stands but the witness is not liable. The author declares this not correct from the Hanafi school because it contradicts the established position of liability. The author then investigates primary sources: he consults al-Muhit by al-Sarakhsi and finds no such detail—it simply supports the general rule. He also refers to Fath al-Qadir, which states that this detailed view was Abu Hanifa's first opinion, which he later retracted in favor of the opinion that the judgment is never overturned and the witnesses are not liable. But the author notes that this is confusing; he then checks al-Kafi and finds that it maintains the liability condition of possession. The discussion shifts to the condition of possession (qabd): some early sources required possession for liability, but the later and relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that liability applies whether or not possession occurred. This is the second opinion of Abu Hanifa and the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The passage also distinguishes between testimony about a specific item ('ayn) and about a debt (dayn): for 'ayn, liability arises even without possession because it is loss of a specific thing; for a debt, liability only arises after possession because the witnesses imposed a debt and must be placed in the same position. Finally, the passage addresses dhimmi witnesses testifying about wine or a pig, which are non-property for Muslims but may be owned by dhimmis. According to Abu Yusuf, they are liable for the value of the pig (since it has value to dhimmis) but not for wine; according to Muhammad, they also guarantee the value of wine. The author presents this as a known intra-Hanafi difference.

Key Terms
الرجوع عن الشهادة (al-ruju' 'an al-shahada): Retraction of testimony; the act of a witness withdrawing his testimony after having given it, which may occur before or after judgment.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability for compensation; here specifically the obligation of the witnesses to pay the value of the property adjudged due to their false testimony.
القبض (al-qabd): Possession; the act of the successful party taking physical control of the property adjudged in his favor.
عين (ayn): Specific property; an identifiable object as opposed to a debt or obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the final Hanafi position (mufta bihi), when are witnesses who retract after judgment liable for the property?
A) Only if the property was a specific item and has been received by the winner.
B) Only if the witnesses are equally reliable at retraction as at the time of testimony.
C) Regardless of whether the property has been received by the winner.
D) They are never liable; only the judge is liable.

Key Takeaway
After judgment, retraction does not invalidate the verdict, but witnesses are liable unconditionally according to the final Hanafi position.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
12 min
Condition of Qabd in Retracting Witnesses' Liability
Discusses whether retracting witnesses are liable only after plaintiff receives property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retracting witnesses' liability, distinguish between cases of specific items ('ayn) and debts (dayn), apply the condition of receipt (qabd), and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Liability for retracting witnesses: unconditional for specific items, conditional on receipt for debts.

When witnesses retract their testimony after a judgment, are they automatically liable? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer, distinguishing between the nature of the property: a specific physical item ('ayn) or a debt (dayn). This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq traces the evolution of Hanafi fatwa on this issue, from an earlier conditional view to a later unconditional one, and clarifies the rational basis using the key distinction from al-Muḥīṭ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon: the liability (ḍamān) of witnesses who retract their testimony after judgment. The hukm level is wājib (obligation to pay compensation), but conditions vary.
The ruling is not simply 'liable' or 'not liable' – it depends on the nature of the testified property.
2
Distinguish between 'ayn and dayn
According to al-Muḥīṭ, if the testimony was for a specific item ('ayn), the witnesses are liable for its value whether the plaintiff received it or not. If it was for a debt (dayn), they are liable only if the plaintiff actually received the debt.
Retraction for an 'ayn is treated as destruction (itlāf), hence unconditional.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta‘līl)
For an 'ayn, the witnesses' retraction is akin to destroying the item – they caused the plaintiff to lose it. For a dayn, they merely imposed a debt obligation; the debt is not actualized until receipt, so liability is conditional.
This is the basis: ḍamān al-rujū‘ is ḍamān itlāf for 'ayn, but not for dayn.
4
Note the intra-Hanafī ikhtilāf
Earlier, Abū Ḥanīfa conditioned liability on receipt even for 'ayn? The text says his later opinion and the two Ṣāḥibayn hold unconditional liability for both? Actually, the unconditional view became muftā bihī. Also, Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad differed on the value of a dhimmī’s wine.
The passage shows evolution: earlier scholars (al-Hidāyah, al-Sarakhsī) conditioned on receipt; later fatwā collections prefer unconditional.
5
Determine the muftā bihī
The relied-upon position for fatwā is unconditional liability (witnesses are liable after judgment whether the plaintiff received the property or not). This is stated in al-Khulāṣah, al-Bazzāziyyah, and Khizānat al-Muftiyīn.
This overrides the earlier conditional view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يتحقق ولأنه لا مماثلة بين أخذ العين وإلزام الدين وقد تبع المصنف صاحب الهداية في تقييده تبعاً للإمام السرخسي وصاحب المجمع وأصحاب الفتاوى في إطلاقهم، فقد صرح في الخلاصة والبزازية وخزانة المفتين بالضمان بعد القضاء قبض المدعي بالمال أو لا قالوا: وعليه الفتوى. وفي الخلاصة إنه قول أبي حنيفة الآخر وهو قولهما ا هـ. وظاهره أنه اشتراط القبض مرجوع عنه. وفرق في المحيط بين العين والدين فقال : شهدا بعين ثم رجعا ضمناً قيمتها قبضها المشهود له أم لا، لأن ضمان الرجوع ضمان إتلاف وضمان الإتلاف مقدر بالمثل إن كان المشهود به مثلياً، وبالقيمة إن لم يكن مثلياً. وإن كان المشهود به ديناً فرجع الشهود قبل قبضه لا يضمنون، وإن قبضه المشهود له ثم رجعا ضمناً لأنهما أوجبا عليه ديناً فيجب في ذمتهما مثل ذلك، ولا يستوفى منهما إلا بعد قبض المشهود به تحقيقاً للمعادلة ا هـ. وهذا قول شيخ الإسلام وشمل أيضاً قوله ما أتلفاه خمر الذمي وخنزيره لكن في كافي الحاكم : وإذا شهد الذميان لذمي بمال أو خمر أو خنزير فقضى القاضي بذلك ثم رجعا ضمناً المال وقيمة الخنزير ولا يضمنان الخمر ولا قيمته في قول أبي يوسف، ويضمنان قيمة الخمر في قول محمد، ولو لم يسلم الشاهدان وأسلم المشهود عليه ثم رجعا عن الشهادة ضمنا قيمة الخنزير ولم يضمنا قيمة الخمر ا هـ .
It is actualized, and because there is no similarity between taking a specific item and imposing a debt. The author followed the author of al-Hidayah in restricting it, following Imam al-Sarakhsi, but the author of al-Majma' and the authors of fatwas were absolute. Indeed, they clearly stated in al-Khulasa, al-Bazzaziyya, and Khizanat al-Muftiyin that after judgment, the witnesses are liable whether or not the plaintiff received the property. They said: and upon it is the fatwa. And in al-Khulasa: it is the other opinion of Abu Hanifa, and it is the opinion of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Its apparent meaning is that the condition of receipt is abandoned. And in al-Muhit, he distinguished between a specific item and a debt: if they testified for a specific item and then retracted, they guarantee its value whether the beneficiary received it or not, because the guarantee of retraction is a guarantee of destruction, and the guarantee of destruction is assessed by the like if the testified item is of a standard type, and by value if not. If the testified matter is a debt and the witnesses retract before receipt, they are not liable; if the beneficiary received it and then they retract, they are liable because they imposed a debt on him, so a similar debt becomes due in their liability, and it is not collected from them except after the receipt of the testified matter to achieve equivalence. This is the statement of Shaykh al-Islam. And it also includes his statement: what they destroyed of a dhimmi's wine and pig. But in Kafi al-Hakim: if two dhimmis testify for a dhimmi for property, wine, or pig, and the judge rules accordingly, then they retract, they are liable for the property and the value of the pig, but they are not liable for the wine or its value according to Abu Yusuf; according to Muhammad, they are liable for the value of the wine. If the two witnesses did not embrace Islam but the judgment debtor embraced Islam, then they retracted the testimony, they are liable for the value of the pig but not for the value of the wine.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the liability of witnesses who retract their testimony after the judge has passed judgment. The core issue is whether liability depends on the plaintiff actually receiving the property (qabd) or not. Some earlier scholars, like the author of al-Hidayah and Imam al-Sarakhsi, conditioned liability on receipt. However, later authorities like the authors of al-Khulasa, al-Bazzaziyya, and Khizanat al-Muftiyin held that witnesses are liable regardless of receipt, and this is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). The text notes that this is also Abu Hanifa's later opinion and the opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Then al-Muhit makes a distinction: if the testimony was for a specific item ('ayn), the witnesses are liable for its value whether the plaintiff received it or not, because retraction is treated as a destruction of the item (damān itlāf). If the testimony was for a debt (dayn), they are only liable if the plaintiff actually received the debt; before receipt, they are not liable because they only imposed a debt, and the debt is not actualized until receipt. The passage also covers the special case of dhimmi witnesses testifying about wine or pig of another dhimmi. According to Abu Yusuf, they are not liable for wine or its value; according to Muhammad, they are liable for its value. The analysis follows the Hanafi methodology of distinguishing between different types of subject matter and applying the principles of liability accordingly.

Key Terms
ضمان الرجوع (damān al-rujū'): Liability incurred by witnesses who retract their testimony after judgment; treated as a guarantee of destruction (damān itlāf) for specific items, and as a debt obligation for debts.
القبض (al-qabd): Physical or legal receipt of the property by the plaintiff as a result of the judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if two witnesses testify that a specific car (an 'ayn) belongs to the plaintiff, and the judge rules accordingly but the plaintiff never takes possession, and the witnesses retract, what is their liability?
A) They are liable because retraction for an 'ayn is unconditional
B) They are not liable because the plaintiff did not receive the car
C) They are liable only if the car is destroyed
D) They are liable only if they retract before judgment

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, retracting witnesses' liability depends on whether the testimony concerned a specific item (unconditional) or a debt (conditional on receipt); the mufta bihi, however, is unconditional for both.

Meaning of Abu Hanifa's Other Opinion on Witness Liability
Clarifies the meaning of Abu Hanifa's 'other opinion' and the hierarchy of sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two interpretations of Abu Hanifa's 'other opinion' on witness liability and identify the mufta bihi position regarding the condition of receipt.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa's 'other opinion' makes witnesses liable even if trustworthy, but does NOT drop the condition of receipt.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a common misconception about Abu Hanifa's second opinion on retracting witnesses. Some scholars interpreted it as unconditional liability, but the commentator shows it only removes the exemption for trustworthy witnesses, not the condition that the plaintiff must have received the property. Understanding this distinction preserves the hierarchy of matn texts over later fatwa collections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested phrase
Locate 'al-qawl al-ākhar' in al-Khulasa. The phrase 'his other opinion' is ambiguous: does it refer to dropping receipt or to the witnesses' state?
The commentator argues the phrase is not explicit; context suggests it refers to the earlier discussion of witnesses' integrity.
2
Understand the two interpretations
Interpretation A (literal reading of al-Khulasa): witnesses always liable upon retraction regardless of receipt. Interpretation B (commentator's view): witnesses liable even if still trustworthy, but receipt remains a condition.
3
Examine the commentator's evidence
The commentator cites al-Fath and al-Walwalijiyya, which explicitly tie the 'other opinion' to the witnesses' state (first opinion: no liability if trustworthy; other opinion: liability even if trustworthy).
These sources are earlier and more detailed than the brief wording in al-Khulasa.
4
Recognize the hierarchical argument
The matn texts (Hidayah, Kanz, etc.) consistently condition liability on receipt. Since the matn authors are pillars of the madhhab, their view takes precedence over later fatwa collections that omit the condition.
This hierarchy is central to Hanafi jurisprudence: zahir al-riwayah over nawadir.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position: witnesses are liable for the property only if the plaintiff received it (for debts). The 'other opinion' only adds that liability applies even if witnesses are still trustworthy.
This reconciles the texts: the condition of receipt stands; the 'other opinion' refines the condition about the witnesses' state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وصاحب المجمع وأصحاب الفتاوى في إطلاقهم كذا في النسخة وهي عبارة غير محررة لأن صاحب المجمع قال في شرحه هذا إذا قبض المدعي المال ديناً كان أو عيناً وأصحاب الفتاوى لم يقيدوا قوله : (وفي الخلاصة أنه قول أبي حنيفة (الآخر) أقول : عبارة الخلاصة هكذا : الشاهدان إذا رجعا عن شهادتهما رجوعاً معتبراً يعني عند القاضي لا يبطل القضاء لكن ضمنا المال الذي شهدا به وهذا قوله الآخر وهو قولهما وعليه الفتوى سواء قبض المقضى له المال الذي قضى له أو لم يقبض انتهت. فقوله وهو قوله الآخر ليس نصاً في رجوعه إلى الإطلاق وإلا لأخره، والذي يظهر لي أنه أراد بقوله الآخر الضمان بالرجوع مطلقاً أي سواء كان الشاهد كحاله الأول في العدالة أو لا، فيكون إشارة إلى ما تقدم الكلام فيه في القولة السابقة يقر به ما في الفتح حيث قال : واعلم أن الشافعية اختلفوا في هذه المسألة والصحيح عند الإمام والعراقيين وغيرهم أن الشهود يضمنون كمذهبنا والقول الآخر لا ينقض ولا يرد المال من المدعي ولا يضمن الشهود وهو عين قول أبي حنيفة الأول إذا كان حالهما وقت الرجوع مثله وقت الأداء .اهـ. وفي الولوالجية : ثم إذا صح الرجوع لا يبطل القضاء ولكن يضمنان المال الذي شهدا له به وهو قولهما وقول أبي حنيفة الآخر اهـ. فهذه العبارة تؤيد ما قلنا ولو سلم أنه أراد رجوع الإمام عن التقييد بالقبض فنقول: لو صح لم يمش على خلافه أصحاب المتون وغيرهم كالهداية والمختار والوقاية والغرر والإصلاح والكنز والمنتقى ومواهب الرحمن، فكلهم قيدوا بالقبض وجزم به صاحب المجمع كما قدمناه والحدادي في الجوهرة، ولو صح نقل الرجوع لذكره شراح الهداية فإنهم اقتصروا على شرح ماذكره الماتن ونقلوا
His statement: (And the author of al-Majma' and the authors of fatwas in their absolute statement such is in the copy, and it is an unrefined expression, because the author of al-Majma' said in his commentary: this is if the plaintiff received the property, whether debt or item, and the authors of fatwas did not restrict it. His statement: (And in al-Khulasa, it is the other opinion of Abu Hanifa) I say: The expression of al-Khulasa is: The two witnesses, if they retract their testimony in a valid manner, meaning before the judge, the judgment is not invalidated, but they are liable for the property they testified to. This is his other opinion, and it is the opinion of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and upon it is the fatwa, whether the judgment beneficiary received the property or not. End. So his statement 'his other opinion' is not explicit that he retracted to the absolute; otherwise he would have delayed it. What appears to me is that by 'the other opinion' he meant the liability upon retraction in an absolute sense, i.e., whether the witness's condition at the time of retraction is like his initial condition of integrity or not. Thus it is an indication to what was discussed earlier in the previous statement, confirmed by what is in al-Fath: Know that the Shafi'is differed on this issue, and the correct view according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) and the Iraqis and others is that the witnesses are liable, like our madhhab, and the other view is that the judgment is not overturned and the money is not returned from the plaintiff and the witnesses are not liable, and this is exactly the first opinion of Abu Hanifa when their condition at the time of retraction is like at the time of testimony. End. And in al-Walwalijiyya: Then if the retraction is valid, the judgment is not invalidated, but they are liable for the money they testified for, and it is the opinion of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and the other opinion of Abu Hanifa. End. These expressions support what we said. Even if we grant that he intended the Imam's retraction from the condition of receipt, we say: if it were correct, the authors of matn and others like al-Hidayah, al-Mukhtar, al-Wiqaya, al-Ghurr, al-Islah, al-Kanz, al-Muntaqa, and Mawāhib al-Rahman would not have acted contrary to it; all of them conditioned on receipt, and the author of al-Majma' affirmed it as we presented, and al-Haddadi in al-Jawhara. And if the transmission of retraction were correct, the commentators of al-Hidayah would have mentioned it, but they confined themselves to explaining what the author mentioned and transmitted.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute clarifying the meaning of Abu Hanifa's 'other opinion' (al-qawl al-ākhar) regarding the liability of retracting witnesses. The commentator notes an ambiguity in the text of al-Khulasa, which says 'this is his other opinion' (huwa qawluhu al-ākhar). Some understood it to mean that Abu Hanifa abandoned the condition of receipt and adopted unconditional liability. However, the commentator argues that the 'other opinion' actually refers to the ruling that witnesses are liable upon retraction regardless of their integrity at the time of retraction, not that the condition of receipt is dropped. He supports this by citing other sources like al-Fath and al-Walwalijiyya, explaining that the first opinion of Abu Hanifa was that witnesses are not liable if they are still trustworthy at retraction, while the other opinion is that they are liable even if trustworthy. The commentator also appeals to the hierarchy of sources: the matn texts (like al-Hidayah, al-Kanz, etc.) consistently condition liability on receipt, and these take precedence over later fatwa collections. Therefore, the condition of receipt remains the relied-upon position for fatwa, contrary to what might be inferred from some fatwa books.

Key Terms
القول الآخر (al-qawl al-ākhar): Abu Hanifa's other opinion on the liability of retracting witnesses; the passage argues it refers to liability even if witnesses are still trustworthy, not to dropping the condition of receipt.
قبض (qabd): Receipt of the subject matter of testimony by the judgment beneficiary, which is a condition for liability in debt cases according to the matn authors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) That witnesses are liable regardless of whether the plaintiff received the property.
B) That witnesses are liable even if they are still trustworthy at the time of retraction.
C) That the judgment is overturned if witnesses retract.
D) That witnesses are not liable at all.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's 'other opinion' on witness liability refines the rule about witness integrity, not receipt; the condition of receipt remains the mufta bihi per the matn tradition.
