No Liability for Retracting Lineage Testimony
Commentary on ruling of no liability for retracting lineage testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when witnesses retract testimony establishing lineage and explain the legal reasoning based on the attribution of inheritance to death.

Core Idea
Testimony about lineage does not create financial liability because lineage is not wealth and inheritance is attributed to death, not the testimony.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from al-Walwalijiyya on retraction of testimony regarding lineage. The Hanafi school holds that witnesses who establish a man's lineage through testimony and then retract are not liable for any financial consequences, whether the retraction occurs during the father's life or after his death. The reasoning engages a fundamental principle: when a legal ruling is based on a cause with two attributes, it is attributed to the last one to occur.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Act and Ruling
Identify the act: retraction of testimony regarding lineage. Determine the ruling: no financial liability on the witnesses.
The act is not about the testimony itself but its retraction after it led to a legal effect.
2
Analyze the Two Temporal Contexts
Distinguish between retraction during the father's life and after his death. During life: testimony was only about lineage, not wealth. After death: inheritance is caused by death, not the testimony.
The text provides separate rationales for each context.
3
Trace the Underlying Legal Maxim
Understand the maxim: 'Every ruling established by a cause with two attributes is attributed to the latter of the two in existence.' Here, inheritance requires both lineage and death; death is the latter, so the ruling is attributed to death.
This maxim prevents imposing liability for events that would have occurred regardless of the testimony.
4
Apply the Maxim to Similar Cases
Recognize that the same reasoning applies to retraction regarding wala' (clientage), kitaba, tadbir, and istilad, as mentioned in the passage.
The commentary groups these together because they share the characteristic of not being purely financial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وأما النسب والولاء والكتابة وأخواها فمع (العتق أي فسنذكرها مع العتق الآتي في كلام المتن والمراد بأخوي الكتابة التدبير والاستيلاد وكأنه رحمه الله تعالى نسي فلم يذكر شيئاً من أحكام النسب والولاء مستقلاً بل ذكر الثلاثة فقط، ولعله اكتفاء بما تضمنته من الولاء والنسب . وفي الولوالجية: ولو ادعى رجل أنه ابن رجل والأب يجحد وأقام البينة أنه ابنه ولد على فراشه فقضي بذلك وأثبت نسبه ثم رجعوا فلا ضمان عليهم سواء رجعوا في حال حياة الأب أو بعد وفاته، أما في حال حياة الأب فلأنهما لم يشهدا على الأب بالمال وإنما شهدا عليه بالنسب والنسب ليس بمال وما ليس بمال لا يضمن بالمال، وأما بعد وفاته فلأنهم لو ضمنوا ما ورث الابن المشهود له لسائر الورثة ولا يجوز ذلك لأن استحقاق الميراث يضاف إلى موت الأب لا إلى النسب لأن الميراث يستحق بالنسب والموت جميعاً والموت آخرهما وجوداً، وكل حكم ثبت بعلة ذات وصفين يضاف إلى آخر الوصفين وجوداً
His statement: (As for lineage, clientage, kitaba and their siblings, they are with (emancipation) meaning we will mention them with the upcoming emancipation in the text. What is meant by the siblings of kitaba are tadbir and istilad. It seems that the author, may Allah have mercy on him, forgot and did not mention anything of the rulings of lineage and clientage independently, but mentioned only the three. Perhaps he sufficed with what they contain of clientage and lineage. And in al-Walwalijiyya: If a man claims to be the son of another and the father denies, and he brings evidence that he is his son born on his bed, and judgment is given and his lineage is established, then the witnesses retract, there is no liability upon them, whether they retract during the father's life or after his death. During the father's life, because they did not testify against the father regarding wealth; they only testified about lineage, and lineage is not wealth, and what is not wealth is not liable for wealth. After his death, because if they were made liable for what the son inherited from the other heirs, that is not permissible because entitlement to inheritance is attributed to the father's death, not to lineage, because inheritance is earned by both lineage and death, and death is the latter of the two in existence. Every ruling established by a cause with two attributes is attributed to the latter of the two in existence.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The commentator explains that the author intended to discuss retraction regarding lineage (nasab), clientage (wala'), and kitaba (contract of manumission) along with their 'siblings'—tadbir (contract to free after death) and istilad (mother of a child). The commentator notes that the author forgot to mention rulings on lineage and clientage independently but covered them indirectly. Then, from al-Walwalijiyya, the ruling is presented: if witnesses establish a man's lineage against a denying father, and then retract, they are not liable for any wealth. During the father's life, the testimony is not about money. After the father's death, liability would mean the witnesses pay the inheritance the son received from the other heirs—but that is invalid because inheritance is caused by both lineage and death; the last cause (death) is the effective one. Since the retraction does not change the death, liability does not attach. The commentator provides a legal maxim: When a ruling has a cause with two attributes, it is attributed to the last in existence.

Key Terms
النسب (al-nasab): Lineage; relationship by blood or marriage.
الولاء (al-wala'): Clientage; the legal relationship between a freed slave and his emancipator.
الكتابة (al-kitaba): A contract of manumission where a slave buys his freedom in installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Walwalijiyya, if witnesses testify that a man is the son of a deceased father, and then retract after the son inherits, are they liable for the inheritance?
A) Yes, because they caused the son to inherit.
B) No, because inheritance is attributed to death, not to their testimony.
C) Yes, but only if the inheritance was more than one-third.
D) No, because the father consented.

Key Takeaway
Witnesses who retract testimony establishing lineage are not liable for any financial consequences because lineage is not wealth and inheritance is legally attributed to death as the final cause.

Liability for Retracting Testimony on Hire and Mudaraba
Rulings on witness retraction in hire and mudaraba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on liability of witnesses who retract testimony regarding hire and mudaraba contracts, distinguishing between cases based on who claimed the hire and whether profit was distributed before retraction.

Core Idea
Liability for retracted testimony on hire depends on who claimed the contract; in mudaraba, it depends on whether profit was taken before retraction.

When witnesses testify about a hire contract or a mudaraba profit share and later retract, their liability for damages is not uniform. The Hanafi school distinguishes several scenarios: in hire, who claimed the hire (hirer or owner) matters; in mudaraba, whether the profit was already distributed. This lesson unpacks the rules from al-Muhit as quoted in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, enabling you to identify the governing conditions for witness liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type and the disputed claim
Read the scenario: is it a hire (ijara) or a mudaraba? In hire, what did the witnesses testify about? In mudaraba, what profit share did they confirm?
The text provides two hire sub-scenarios and two mudaraba sub-scenarios.
2
Determine who claimed the contract and who denied
For hire, note whether the hirer or the owner claimed the contract. The liability rule flips depending on this.
If the hirer claimed hire and owner denied, witnesses are not liable for the excess. If owner claimed and hirer denied, they are liable.
3
Assess whether property damage occurred and whether hire was collected
In the first hire scenario, the camel was injured and the owner had taken some hire. Liability is the camel's value minus the hire taken.
This is an exception: the owner's receipt reduces the witnesses' liability.
4
For mudaraba, check if profit was distributed before retraction
If the profit was not yet received and divided, witnesses are not liable. If they had taken half each, they must repay the excess (one-sixth of the profit).
Profit obtained after retraction is treated differently depending on whether capital was merchandise or cash.
5
Apply the specific rule to the facts
Match the given scenario to one of the described cases and state the witnesses' liability (amount and conditions).
The text from al-Muhit is relied upon (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الإجارة ففي المحيط ركب بعير الرجل إلى مكة يدعي الإجارة بخمسين وأقام بينة فعطب وادعى صاحب البعير الغصب ثم رجعا ضمنا قيمة البعير يوم عطب إلا مقدار ما أخذ صاحب البعير من الأجر شهدا أنه أكراه دابته بمائة إلى موضع كذا وأجر مثلها مائتان فركبها ثم رجعا لم يضمنا الفضل إن ادعى المستأجر الإجارة وجحد صاحب الدابة، وإن ادعاها صاحب الإبل وجحد المستأجر ضمنا له ما أداه ما فوق أجر البعير. وأما المضاربة ففي المحيط ادعى المضارب نصف الربح فشهدا به ورب المال مقر بالثلث ثم رجعا والربح لم يقبض لم يضمنا، فإن قبضاه واقتسماه نصفين ثم رجعا ضمنا سدس الربح؛ قيل هذا في كل ربح حصل قبل رجوعهما، فأما ربح حصل بعد رجوعهما فإن كان رأس المال عرضاً فكذلك وإن كان نقداً فرب المال يملك فسخها فكان راضياً باستحقاق الربح ا هـ
As for hire, in al-Muhit: A man rode another's camel to Mecca, claiming hire for fifty, and brought evidence, then the camel was injured. The camel owner claimed usurpation, then they retracted: they are liable for the value of the camel on the day it was injured except for the amount the camel owner took as hire. They testified that he leased his animal for one hundred to such place, while the fair hire is two hundred, and he rode it, then they retracted: they are not liable for the excess if the hirer claimed the hire and the animal owner denied. But if the camel owner claimed the hire and the hirer denied, they are liable for what he paid above the hire of the camel. As for mudaraba, in al-Muhit: The mudarib claimed half the profit, two witnesses testified to that, while the capital owner admitted one third. Then they retracted, and the profit had not been received: they are not liable. If they had received and divided it in half, then retracted, they are liable for one-sixth of the profit. It is said this applies to any profit obtained before their retraction. As for profit obtained after their retraction, if the capital was merchandise, same rule; if it was cash, the capital owner has the right to rescind, so he is considered content with the entitlement to profit.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage covers two topics: hire (ijara) and mudaraba (mudaraba). For ijara, two scenarios are given. In the first, a man claims he hired a camel for fifty and brings witnesses; the camel is injured, and the owner claims it was usurped. If the witnesses retract, they are liable for the camel's value minus the hire amount the owner collected. In the second, the witness testifies that the animal was leased for a price (100) while fair hire is 200. If the hirer claims hire and owner denies, witnesses are not liable for the excess; but if the owner claims hire and hirer denies, they are liable for the excess paid. For mudaraba, if witnesses testify that the mudarib is entitled to half the profit but capital owner admits only one third, and they retract before any profit distribution, they are not liable. If they had already distributed half each, they are liable for one-sixth. For profit after retraction, if capital was merchandise, same; if cash, the capital owner can rescind, so he is deemed satisfied.

Key Terms
الإجارة (al-ijara): Hire; a contract for using an asset or services in exchange for payment.
المضاربة (al-mudaraba): A profit-sharing partnership where one party provides capital and the other labor.
الرجوع (al-ruju'): Retraction; withdrawing a previously given testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a mudaraba, witnesses testify that the mudarib is entitled to half the profit, but the capital owner admits only one-third. They retract after the profit of 60 dinars has been received and divided equally (30 each). What is the witnesses' liability?
A) They are not liable because profit was earned.
B) They are liable for 5 dinars (one-sixth of 30).
C) They are liable for 10 dinars (one-sixth of 60).
D) They are liable for 15 dinars.

Key Takeaway
Liability for retracted testimony in hire and mudaraba hinges on who claimed the contract and whether profits were distributed before retraction.

Retraction Concerning Mudaraba Profit Shares
Ruling on liability for retracting testimony about mudaraba profit shares

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on liability of witnesses who retract testimony about mudaraba profit shares in scenarios involving received vs. unrealized profit and cash vs. merchandise capital.

Core Idea
Retracting witnesses are liable only if profit was actually distributed based on their false testimony.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from al-Muhit regarding witnesses who testify in a mudaraba dispute and then retract. The ruling hinges on whether the profit was received and distributed before retraction, and on the nature of the capital (cash or merchandise). Understanding this case illustrates how Hanafi fiqh balances evidentiary fairness against protection of actual losses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial scenario
The mudarib claims half the profit, the capital owner admits only one third. Two witnesses testify in favor of the mudarib's claim. Then the witnesses retract their testimony.
This is a dispute about profit shares, not about existence of the mudaraba.
2
Check if profit was received before retraction
If the profit had not yet been received (e.g., still in the business), the witnesses are not liable regardless of their false testimony. If the profit was already received and divided equally (half each), liability arises.
Liability attaches only when the false testimony caused actual transfer of funds.
3
Calculate the amount of liability
The mudarib was entitled to only one third (as admitted by the owner) but received half. The excess is half minus one third = one sixth of the profit. The witnesses are liable jointly for this one sixth.
Each witness is liable for half of the excess if joint liability applies; the text implies joint liability.
4
Distinguish profit earned after retraction
For profit earned after the witnesses retracted, the rule depends on the type of capital: if merchandise (urud), liability is same as above; if cash (naqd), the capital owner has the right to rescind the mudaraba, so he is deemed to have consented to the mudarib's entitlement, making witnesses not liable.
The difference is that with cash, the owner could have terminated the contract and avoided the dispute.
5
Extract the underlying principle
Witnesses are only liable for losses actually caused by their testimony that the claimant relied upon to his detriment. The owner's power to rescind (in cash cases) negates causation.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle that liability follows causation (al-ghurm bi al-ghunm).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المضاربة ففي المحيط ادعى المضارب نصف الربح فشهدا به ورب المال مقر بالثلث ثم رجعا والربح لم يقبض لم يضمنا، فإن قبضاه واقتسماه نصفين ثم رجعا ضمنا سدس الربح؛ قيل هذا في كل ربح حصل قبل رجوعهما، فأما ربح حصل بعد رجوعهما فإن كان رأس المال عرضاً فكذلك وإن كان نقداً فرب المال يملك فسخها فكان راضياً باستحقاق الربح ا هـ
As for mudaraba, in al-Muhit: The mudarib claimed half the profit, two witnesses testified to that, while the capital owner admitted one third. Then they retracted, and the profit had not been received: they are not liable. If they had received and divided it in half, then retracted, they are liable for one-sixth of the profit. It is said this applies to any profit obtained before their retraction. As for profit obtained after their retraction, if the capital was merchandise, same rule; if it was cash, the capital owner has the right to rescind, so he is considered content with the entitlement to profit.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit details retraction in mudaraba. The mudarib claims half the profit; the capital owner admits only one third. Two witnesses support the mudarib. If they retract before any profit distribution, they are not liable because the mudarib hasn't taken anything. If they had already received and divided the profit equally (half each), they are liable for the excess: one-sixth (since the correct share was one third for the mudarib, but they testified for half, so the excess is half minus one third = one-sixth). For profit that accrues after retraction, if the capital was merchandise (urud), the same rule applies. If it was cash (naqd), the capital owner can rescind the mudaraba, so he is deemed to have consented to the profit entitlement, and thus witnesses are not liable for that post-retraction profit.

Key Terms
المضاربة (al-mudaraba): A profit-sharing partnership; capital owner provides funds, mudarib provides labor.
الربح (al-ribh): Profit; the earnings from the mudaraba.
الرجوع عن الشهادة (al-ruju' 'an al-shahada): Retraction of testimony; witnesses withdraw their previously given statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a mudaraba, witnesses testify that the mudarib gets half the profit, while the capital owner admits one third. The profit is later earned but not yet distributed. Then the witnesses retract. What is their liability?
A) They are liable for one-sixth of the profit.
B) They are not liable.
C) They are liable for the entire half.
D) They are liable only if the capital was cash.

Key Takeaway
Witnesses retracting testimony about mudaraba profit are liable only for the excess actually distributed before retraction; post-retraction profit liability depends on the owner's power to rescind the contract.

Liability for Retracting Testimony in Partnership
Rulings on liability for retracting testimony about partnership contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the liability of witnesses who retract testimony in a partnership contract and distinguish between profits divided before and after testimony.

Core Idea
Witnesses who retract are liable only for profits actually distributed as a direct result of their testimony.

This passage from al-Muhit and Kafi al-Hakim addresses a specific scenario: witnesses testify about a partnership profit-sharing arrangement, then retract. The ruling clarifies that their liability is limited to the excess profit that was actually paid out based on their false testimony; later profits are not their responsibility. It also covers a case where testimony leads to a court order transferring property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
The passage gives two distinct rulings: one from al-Muhit about profit shares and retraction after division, and one from Kafi al-Hakim about a mufawada partnership where property was awarded based on testimony.
Each scenario has its own liability rule.
2
Analyze the First Scenario (Profit Shares)
Two witnesses testify that partners agreed on equal capital but profit shares: one claims half, but true share is one third. They had already made profit and divided it before retraction. The witnesses are liable for the difference between half and one third.
Liability is only for the excess that was actually taken due to false testimony.
3
Analyze the Second Scenario (Property Transfer)
A witness testifies that money in another's possession belongs to both as a mufawada partnership. The court awards half to the claimant. Upon retraction, the witnesses are liable for that half to the defendant.
Liability covers the property directly transferred by court order based on the testimony.
4
Derive the General Principle
Witnesses are liable only for the actual loss caused by their testimony: either the excess profit divided or the property awarded. Profit earned after the testimony is not their responsibility because it was not caused by their testimony.
Causation (direct link) is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الشركة ففي المحيط : شهدا أنهما اشتركا ورأس مال كل واحد منهما ألف على أن الربح أثلاث وصاحب الثلث يدعي النصف وربحا قبل الشهادة فاقتسما ثم رجعا ضمناً لصاحب الثلث ما بين النصف والثلث وما ربحا بعد الشهادة فلا يضمنان عليهما ا هـ . وفي كافي الحاكم في يد رجل مال فشهد الرجل أنه شريكه شركة مفاوضة فقضى له بنصف ما في يديه ثم رجعا ضمنا ذلك النصف للمشهود عليه.
As for partnership, in al-Muhit: They testified that they entered into a partnership, each with a capital of one thousand, with profit divided in thirds, but the one entitled to one third claimed half. They made profit before the testimony and divided it. Then they retracted: they are liable to the partner entitled to one third for the difference between half and one third. As for profit made after the testimony, they are not liable for it. And in Kafi al-Hakim: A man had money in his hand, and another testified that he was his partner in a partnership of mutual agency (mufawada), so the judge ruled that the claimant gets half of what was in his hands. Then they retracted; they are liable for that half to the defendant.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit and Kafi al-Hakim covers retraction in partnership (sharika). In the first case, two partners claim they had a partnership with equal capital but profit shares: one claims one third, the other claims half. They had already made profit and divided it based on the testimony. Then the witnesses retract: they are liable for the excess that the one-third partner took (the difference between half and one third). Profit made after the testimony is not subject to liability because it was not caused by their testimony. In the second case from Kafi al-Hakim: someone testifies that the money in another's possession belongs to both as a mufawada partnership. The judge awards half to the claimant. After retraction, the witnesses are liable for that half to the defendant.

Key Terms
الشركة (al-sharika): Partnership; a contract where two or more share capital and profits.
المفاوضة (al-mufawada): A partnership with full mutual agency and equal capital and liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a partnership case, witnesses testify that profit shares are equal, but actually one partner is entitled to one third. They had already divided profit before the testimony, then retract. What are the witnesses liable for?
A) All profit ever earned.
B) The excess between what was taken and the true share.
C) Nothing, because the division was before testimony.
D) They are liable to the defendant only.

Key Takeaway
Witnesses who retract are liable only for the excess profit or property that was actually transferred as a direct result of their testimony.

Liability for Retracting Testimony in Pre-emption
Rulings on liability for retracting testimony about pre-emption claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witness liability when retracting testimony in pre-emption cases and distinguish between liability for the property and liability for improvements.

Core Idea
Witnesses who retract after a pre-emption ruling are liable only for improvements they caused to be destroyed, not the property itself.

When witnesses testify that a property belongs to a pre-emptor and the judge rules accordingly, their retraction has different consequences depending on whether the original buyer made improvements. This lesson explores a ruling from al-Muhit that clarifies when witnesses are liable and when they are not. Understanding this nuance is essential for applying the Hanafi position correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases in the passage
The passage presents two scenarios: one where the original buyer did not build, and one where he built and the judge ordered demolition. Note the ruling for each.
The key difference is the presence of improvements (building) that were destroyed due to the testimony.
2
Apply the ruling to the first case (no building)
If the witnesses retract and the buyer did not build, they are not liable for the house itself. The pre-emptor paid for it, so no loss was caused by the testimony.
This is because the house ownership transfer is considered valid despite the retraction.
3
Apply the ruling to the second case (with building)
If the buyer built and the judge ordered demolition, the witnesses are liable for the value of the building. They also have the right to demolish it themselves.
The liability arises because the testimony directly caused the demolition of the building, which is a tangible loss.
4
Understand the underlying principle
Witnesses are liable for actual damages they cause (the building), but not for the property itself because the pre-emptor's ownership was established by the court and the price was paid.
This distinguishes between direct and indirect causation in liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الشفعة ففي المحيط : ولو شهدا أن الدار التي في يد الشفيع ملكه فقضى له بالشفعة ثم رجعا لم يضمنا، وإن كان الأول قد بنى فأمره القاضي بنقضه يضمنان قيمة بنائه ولهما النقض ا هـ
As for pre-emption, in al-Muhit: If they testify that the house in the hand of the pre-emptor is his property, and the judge rules for pre-emption, then they retract, they are not liable. But if the first (original buyer) had built on it and the judge ordered its demolition, they are liable for the value of his building, and they have the right to demolish.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage addresses retraction in pre-emption (shuf'a). If witnesses testify that the house claimed by the pre-emptor is indeed his, and the judge grants pre-emption, then they retract—they are not liable for the house itself because the pre-emptor paid for it. However, if the original buyer (the one from whom the property was taken) had made improvements (built on it) and the judge ordered demolition, the witnesses are liable for the value of those improvements. They also have the right to demolish the building themselves.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'a): Pre-emption; the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase property when it is sold to a third party.
النقض (al-naqd): Demolition; here, the tearing down of a building built by the original buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Witnesses testify that a house belongs to the pre-emptor, and the judge rules for pre-emption. The original buyer had built a structure. The witnesses retract. What are they liable for?
A) The value of the house.
B) The value of the structure built by the buyer.
C) They are not liable for anything.
D) They are liable for the pre-emption price.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, witnesses who retract after a pre-emption ruling are liable only for improvements they caused to be demolished, not the property itself.

Witness Liability for Retracting False Inheritance Testimony
Ruling on liability when witnesses retract false inheritance testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when witnesses retract false testimony about a deceased's religion and identify the party entitled to compensation.

Core Idea
False testimony about religion can alter inheritance; retraction makes witnesses liable to the rightful heir.

Inheritance rules rest on fixed religious distinctions: a Muslim cannot inherit from a non-Muslim, and vice versa. When witnesses testify falsely about a father's Muslim status, they can cause a wrongful transfer of wealth. This lesson examines a case from al-Muhit where witnesses retract such testimony, leading to personal liability. Understanding this ruling reinforces the principle that testimony affecting rights is not consequence-free.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core factual scenario
Read the passage and list the key facts: who testified, what they claimed, the known reality, and the other heir's religion.
The father was known to be a non-Muslim, but witnesses claimed he died Muslim.
2
Determine the legal effect of the false testimony
Understand why the Muslim son inherits initially: the court relies on testimony. But the truth is different, so the inheritance is wrongful.
Hanafi law: Muslim cannot inherit from non-Muslim, so the Muslim son should not have inherited.
3
Analyze the retraction and liability
After retraction, the witnesses become liable. Identify who the compensation goes to and why.
Compensation goes to the disbelieving son (the legitimate heir), not to the state.
4
Extract the governing principle
State the general rule: witnesses who cause a financial transfer by false testimony and then retract must restore the property to the rightful owner.
This aligns with the maxim 'al-ghurmu bil-ghunmi' (liability with gain) but here it's a penalty for falsehood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الميراث ففي المحيط : شهد الرجل مسلم أن أباه مات مسلماً وعرف كافراً وللميت ابن آخر كافر ثم رجعوا ضمنوا الميراث للكافر الوارث.
As for inheritance, in al-Muhit: A Muslim man testified that his father died a Muslim, while known to be a disbeliever, and the deceased had another son who was a disbeliever. Then they retracted: they are liable for the inheritance to the disbelieving heir.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This short passage from al-Muhit covers retraction in inheritance. A Muslim man claims his father died Muslim (so he can inherit), but the father was known to be a disbeliever. The deceased also has a disbelieving son (the other heir). The witnesses support the Muslim's claim. After judgment, they retract. They become liable to pay the inheritance (that the Muslim took) to the disbelieving son, who is the true heir because the father died a non-Muslim (so Muslim cannot inherit from non-Muslim).

Key Terms
الميراث (al-mirath): Inheritance; property inherited from a deceased person.
الرجوع (al-ruju'): Retraction; withdrawing previously given testimony.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability; obligation to compensate for loss or damage.
الكافر الوارث (al-kafir al-warith): The disbelieving heir; the legitimate inheritor who is not Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case from al-Muhit, after the witnesses retract, who is entitled to compensation from the witnesses?
A) The Muslim son who inherited.
B) The non-Muslim son (the disbelieving heir).
C) The state treasury (bayt al-mal).
D) The witnesses themselves keep it as they retracted.

Key Takeaway
False testimony about a deceased's religion that leads to wrongful inheritance makes the witnesses personally liable to the true heir if they retract.

Liability for Retracting Testimony in Will Cases
Ruling on witness liability for retraction in will-related testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for witnesses who retract testimony in will cases, and distinguish between bequest and executor appointment scenarios.

Core Idea
Witnesses who retract after testifying to a bequest must pay; witnesses of executor appointment bear no liability for the executor's actions.

This passage from al-Muhit and Kafi al-Hakim presents two distinct cases of witness retraction in will (wasiyya) matters. Understanding when liability attaches is crucial for correctly applying Hanafi rules on testimony and compensation. We will break down each scenario and its legal consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note that it discusses two separate cases: (1) witnesses of a bequest and (2) witnesses of executor appointment.
2
Case 1: witnesses of a bequest
A man claims the deceased willed him one-third of his estate. Witnesses testify, judgment is given, then they retract. Ruling: they are liable for the full amount of the bequest.
The phrase 'ضمنوا جميع وتمامه' indicates liability for the entire bequest.
3
Case 2: witnesses of executor appointment
Witnesses testify that the deceased appointed a specific person as executor. The judge confirms, then they retract. Ruling: no liability on the witnesses; only the executor is liable if he consumed anything.
The text says 'فلا ضمان عليهما والضمان على الوصي'.
4
Analyze the distinction
Why the difference? In the bequest case, the testimony directly caused the legatee to receive property. In the appointment case, the testimony only established the executor's authority; any subsequent loss is due to the executor's own actions, not the testimony.
Liability attaches only when the retracted testimony directly caused a transfer of property.
5
Apply the principle
Given a new scenario, determine whether witnesses are liable based on whether their testimony directly caused a property transfer or just a status.
Practice applying to hypothetical cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الوصية ففي المحيط : ادعى رجل أن فلاناً الميت أوصى له بالثلث من كل شيء وأقام البينة فقضى ثم رجعوا ضمنوا جميع وتمامه فيه. وفي كافي الحاكم لو شهدا أن الميت أوصى إلى هذا في تركته فقضى القاضي بذلك ثم رجعا فلا ضمان عليهما والضمان على الوصي إن استهلك شيئاً ! اهـ.
As for the will, in al-Muhit: A man claimed that so-and-so the deceased willed to him one third of everything, and he brought evidence, and judgment was given, then they retracted: they are liable for all of it, and the completion is in it. And in Kafi al-Hakim: If they testified that the deceased appointed this person as executor over his estate, and the judge ruled accordingly, then they retracted: there is no liability on them, and the liability is on the executor if he consumed anything.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage from al-Muhit and Kafi al-Hakim covers retraction in wills (wasiyya). In the first case, a man claims he was bequeathed one third of the estate, and witnesses support him. After judgment, they retract: they are liable for the entire one third (the full amount the legatee received). The phrase 'جميع وتمامه فيه' indicates they are liable for the whole bequest. In the second case from Kafi al-Hakim, if witnesses testify that the deceased appointed a certain person as executor (wasi), and the judge confirms, then they retract: they are not liable for any estate consumed by the executor; only the executor is liable.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyya): Will; a bequest of property or appointment of an executor after death.
الوصي (al-wasi): Executor; a person appointed to manage the estate after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Witnesses testify that a deceased person appointed a certain man as executor. After the executor consumes part of the estate, the witnesses retract. According to Kafi al-Hakim, who is liable for the consumed property?
A) The witnesses.
B) The executor.
C) The legatee.
D) The judge.

Key Takeaway
Witnesses are liable for a retracted bequest but not for an executor's misconduct.

Retraction of Testimony on Deposit and Loan
Ruling on witness liability after retraction in deposit/loan cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witnesses who retract after causing liability in deposit or loan cases and explain who must compensate whom.

Core Idea
Retracting witnesses must repay the defendant if their testimony caused him to pay.

Witnesses sometimes recant their testimony after a judgment has been executed. This lesson addresses a specific scenario from the Hanafi work Kafi al-Hakim: witnesses testify that a defendant holds a deposit or loan, the defendant denies but the judge rules against him, and after payment the witnesses retract. The ruling is clear: the witnesses must compensate the defendant for what he paid, shifting the burden from the wronged defendant to the witnesses who caused the harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The case involves witnesses testifying that a person has a deposit (wadi'a) or a loan for use (ariya) belonging to someone else. The defendant denies the claim, but the judge accepts the testimony and orders the defendant to pay the value.
The defendant initially denies, so the testimony alone caused the judgment against him.
2
Recognize the retraction event
After the defendant pays, the witnesses retract their testimony. Retraction means they admit their earlier statement was false.
Retraction can occur at any time, but here it happens after the judgment has been executed.
3
State the ruling on liability
According to Kafi al-Hakim, the witnesses become liable to the defendant for the amount he paid. The phrase 'ضمنا له ما غرم' means they must reimburse him exactly what he lost.
This is a wujub (obligation) on the witnesses; it is wajib for them to pay.
4
Apply the same rule to loan (ariya)
The passage explicitly states that the same ruling applies to 'ariya (loan for use). The reasoning is identical: the witnesses caused the defendant to pay based on false testimony, so they must compensate.
Both deposit and loan for use are contracts of trust, and the ruling is consistent for both.
5
Understand the underlying principle
The principle is that witnesses who cause harm through false testimony must make good the loss. When they retract, they admit fault, and liability shifts from the defendant to them.
This aligns with the broader Hanafi rule that retraction of testimony can create liability for the retractors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الوديعة والعارية ففي كافي الحاكم : شهدا على رجل بوديعة فجحدها فضمنها إياه القاضي ثم رجعا ضمنا له ما غرم وكذلك العارية ا هـ
As for deposit and loan, in Kafi al-Hakim: They testified against a man for a deposit, and he denied it, and the judge held him liable for it. Then they retracted: they are liable to him for what he paid. And similarly for a loan.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This brief passage from Kafi al-Hakim covers retraction in cases of deposit (wadi'a) and loan (ariya). If witnesses testify that a man holds a deposit (or loan) for another, and the defendant denies, but the judge rules against him (makes him liable for the value), then the witnesses retract—they become liable to pay the defendant the amount he was forced to pay. The same ruling applies to 'ariya (loan for use).

Key Terms
الوديعة (al-wadi'a): Deposit; property left with someone for safekeeping.
العارية (al-ariya): Loan for use; property given to someone to use temporarily without payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, after witnesses retract in a deposit case, who is liable to pay the defendant?
A) The plaintiff (depositor) must return the money.
B) The judge is liable for the wrong judgment.
C) The witnesses must compensate the defendant.
D) The defendant must forfeit because he admitted payment.

Key Takeaway
Retracting witnesses who caused the defendant to pay must reimburse him fully, as liability shifts from the defendant to the witnesses.

Partial Retraction of Witnesses: How a Ruling Can Persist with Part of Its Cause
Expansion of the rule on witness retraction with qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when one witness retracts and explain the qiyas (analogy) used to justify partial persistence of the ruling.

Core Idea
A ruling can persist with part of its cause, even if it could not be established with only that part.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the ruling when one of two witnesses retracts. It introduces a key Hanafi principle: that a ruling established by a complete cause can partially remain if part of the cause is removed, drawing an analogy from zakat law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for retraction of one witness
State the Hanafi position: if one of two witnesses retracts, the remaining witness's testimony supports half the claim, and the retractor is liable for that half.
The text says 'ضمن النصف' (liable for half) and 'العبرة لمن بقي' (consideration is for the one who remains).
2
Understand the objection
Recognize the counterargument: some might say that since the ruling was established by the complete testimony (both witnesses), if part of the cause is removed, the whole ruling should collapse.
The objection is phrased as 'لا يقال... فوجب أن لا تبقى به أيضاً' (do not say... so it should not remain by it either).
3
Locate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that a ruling can remain by part of the cause even if it could not be initially established by that part. The proof is the qiyas to the zakat year (hawl) and nisab.
The year begins with full nisab, but if nisab decreases, the year continues with the remaining portion.
4
Apply the analogy to the witness scenario
Just as the zakat year persists with partial nisab, the judgment in testimony persists with partial evidence (one witness). The ruling is not fully established by one witness initially, but once established by two, it can remain with one.
This is an example of qiyas khafi, drawing an underlying commonality (illa) of partial cause sustaining a pre-established ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن رجع أحدهما ضمن النصف والعبرة لمن بقي لا لمن رجع) يعني وقد بقي من يبقى بشهادته نصف الحق ولا يقال لا يجوز أن يثبت الحكم ببعض العلة فوجب أن لا تبقى به أيضاً لأنا نقول : يجوز أن يبقى الحكم ببعض العلة وإن لم يثبت به ابتداء كالحول المنعقد على النصاب يبقى ببقاء بعض النصاب وإن لم ينعقد به ابتداء ومن مسائل الجامع الكبير : أربعة
His statement: (If one of the two retracts, he is liable for half, and the consideration is for the one who remains, not the one who retracts.) That is, the one who remains with his testimony sustains half the right. And do not say that a ruling cannot be established by part of the cause, so it cannot remain by it either; for we say: It is permissible for a ruling to remain by part of the cause, even if it was not initially established by it, like the year (hawl) that began upon the nisab: it remains with the survival of part of the nisab, even if it did not begin with it. And from the issues of al-Jami' al-Kabir: four...
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the principle when one of two witnesses retracts. The teacher states that if one retracts, the remaining witness's testimony can still support half of the claim. This is justified by an analogy: just as the year (for zakat) begins when the full nisab is present, but if part of the nisab remains, the count continues even if it didn't start with just that part. Similarly, a ruling can be established by a complete cause, but it can persist with a part. The text then refers to al-Jami' al-Kabir for examples (indicating four cases).

Key Terms
العلة (al-illa): The effective cause; here the complete testimony is the `illa for the judgment.
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum amount of wealth liable for zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two witnesses testify that someone owes 1000. One witness retracts. According to the principle stated, what is the effect?
A) The entire judgment becomes invalid.
B) Half the claim (500) stands, and the retracting witness is liable for that half.
C) The remaining witness must also retract.
D) The judgment is reduced to 250.

Key Takeaway
Partial retraction of one witness does not nullify the judgment; the remaining witness supports half the claim, and the retractor is liable.

15 min
General Rule and Specific Cases of Witness Retraction
Matn rulings on witness retraction across contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on witness retraction and apply it to determine liability in various contractual contexts.

Core Idea
Retracting witnesses are liable only if their retraction causes actual loss; the testimony of remaining witnesses stands.

This lesson presents the Hanafi position on witness retraction (الرجوع عن الشهادة) after judgment. The key principle is that consideration is given to the witnesses who maintain their testimony, not to those who retract. Liability (الضمان) is imposed only when retraction causes a loss that cannot be compensated by the remaining testimony. The lesson then applies this principle across multiple contracts: hire, mudaraba, partnership, pre-emption, inheritance, bequest, deposit, and loan.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
The text opens with: 'العبرة لمن بقي لا لمن رجع' (consideration is for those who remain, not for those who retract). Retraction alone does not impose liability.
This is the foundational maxim for all subsequent cases.
2
Apply the rule to the three-witness scenario
If three witnesses testify and one retracts, the retracting witness is not liable because the other two sustain the judgment.
3
Identify the condition for liability
Liability (daman) arises only when retraction causes loss to a party. Each specific case tests this condition.
For example, in hire, if the animal perishes and witnesses retract, they guarantee the value minus the hire paid.
4
Study the exceptions and nuances
In mudaraba, if profit is not yet taken, retraction incurs no liability. In pre-emption, retraction does not make witnesses liable for the property, but if the pre-emptor built, they guarantee the building's value.
Note the distinction between liability for the principal right and for consequential damages.
5
Synthesize the pattern
Liability is measured by the loss actually caused. In all cases, the witnesses are liable to the extent the litigant suffered due to their retraction.
Memorize the key Arabic phrases for each contract: they serve as anchors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادات باب الرجوع عن الشهادة
النصف والعبرة لمن بقي لا لمن رجع فإن شهد ثلاثة ورجع واحد لم يضمن وإن رجع أثلاثاً.
يدعي الإجارة بخمسين وأقام بينة فعطب وادعى صاحب البعير الغصب ثم رجعا ضمنا قيمة البعير يوم عطب إلا مقدار ما أخذ صاحب البعير من الأجر شهدا أنه أكراه دابته بمائة إلى موضع كذا وأجر مثلها مائتان فركبها ثم رجعا لم يضمنا الفضل إن ادعى المستأجر الإجارة وجحد صاحب الدابة، وإن ادعاها صاحب الإبل وجحد المستأجر ضمنا له ما أداه ما فوق أجر البعير. وأما المضاربة ففي المحيط ادعى المضارب نصف الربح فشهدا به ورب المال مقر بالثلث ثم رجعا والربح لم يقبض لم يضمنا، فإن قبضاه واقتسماه نصفين ثم رجعا ضمنا سدس الربح؛ قيل هذا في كل ربح حصل قبل رجوعهما، فأما ربح حصل بعد رجوعهما فإن كان رأس المال عرضاً فكذلك وإن كان نقداً فرب المال يملك فسخها فكان راضياً باستحقاق الربح ا هـ . وأما الشركة ففي المحيط : شهدا أنهما اشتركا ورأس مال كل واحد منهما ألف على أن الربح أثلاث وصاحب الثلث يدعي النصف وربحا قبل الشهادة فاقتسما ثم رجعا ضمناً لصاحب الثلث ما بين النصف والثلث وما ربحا بعد الشهادة فلا يضمنان عليهما ا هـ . وفي كافي الحاكم في يد رجل مال فشهد الرجل أنه شريكه شركة مفاوضة فقضى له بنصف ما في يديه ثم رجعا ضمنا ذلك النصف للمشهود عليه. وأما الشفعة ففي المحيط : ولو شهدا أن الدار التي في يد الشفيع ملكه فقضى له بالشفعة ثم رجعا لم يضمنا، وإن كان الأول قد بنى فأمره القاضي بنقضه يضمنان قيمة بنائه ولهما النقض ا هـ . وأما الميراث ففي المحيط : شهد الرجل مسلم أن أباه مات مسلماً وعرف كافراً وللميت ابن آخر كافر ثم رجعوا ضمنوا الميراث للكافر الوارث. وأما الوصية ففي المحيط : ادعى رجل أن فلاناً الميت أوصى له بالثلث من كل شيء وأقام البينة فقضى ثم رجعوا ضمنوا جميع وتمامه فيه. وفي كافي الحاكم لو شهدا أن الميت أوصى إلى هذا في تركته فقضى القاضي بذلك ثم رجعا فلا ضمان عليهما والضمان على الوصي إن استهلك شيئاً ! اهـ. وأما الوديعة والعارية ففي كافي الحاكم : شهدا على رجل بوديعة فجحدها فضمنها إياه القاضي ثم رجعا ضمنا له ما غرم وكذلك العارية ا هـ .
Book of Testimonies, Chapter of Retraction from Testimony. Half, and consideration is for those who remain, not for those who retract. If three testify and one retracts, he is not liable; if he retracts with a third [of the amount]… One claims hire for fifty and produces evidence, then the animal perishes and the owner claims usurpation, then they retract: they guarantee the value of the animal on the day it perished except the amount the owner took from the hire. Two testify that he leased his animal for one hundred to such a place, while its hire is two hundred, and he rode it; then they retract: they do not guarantee the excess if the hirer claims the hire and the owner denies. If the owner claims it and the hirer denies, they guarantee to him what he paid above the hire of the animal. As for mudaraba, in al-Muhit: the mudarib claims half the profit, two testify to that while the owner admits a third; then they retract, and the profit has not been taken: they are not liable. If they took it and divided it in half, then retracted, they guarantee one-sixth of the profit. It is said this applies to every profit obtained before their retraction. As for profit obtained after their retraction, if the capital is goods, it is the same; if it is cash, then the owner has the right to annul the contract, so he is considered satisfied with the entitlement to the profit. As for partnership, in al-Muhit: two testify that they entered into partnership with each having a capital of one thousand, profit in thirds; the one entitled to one-third claims half, and they profit before the testimony, then divide it; then they retract: they guarantee to the one entitled to one-third the difference between half and one-third. What they profit after the testimony, they do not guarantee. In Kafi al-Hakim: A man has property in his hand, and another testifies that he is his partner in a partnership of mutual agency; the judge rules for him half of what is in his hand; then they retract: they guarantee that half to the defendant. As for pre-emption, in al-Muhit: If two testify that the house in the hand of the pre-emptor is his property, and the judge rules for him pre-emption, then they retract: they do not guarantee. But if the owner had built and the judge ordered him to demolish, they guarantee the value of his building, and he may demolish. As for inheritance, in al-Muhit: Muslim men testify that his father died a Muslim, while he is known to be a disbeliever, and the deceased has another son who is a disbeliever; then they retract: they guarantee the inheritance to the disbelieving heir. As for bequest, in al-Muhit: A man claims that so-and-so the deceased bequeathed to him one-third of everything, and he produces evidence; the judge rules; then they retract: they guarantee all of it. In Kafi al-Hakim: If two testify that the deceased appointed this person as executor over his estate, and the judge rules accordingly, then they retract: there is no guarantee on them; the guarantee is on the executor if he consumes anything. As for deposit and loan, in Kafi al-Hakim: Two testify against a man concerning a deposit; he denies it; the judge holds him liable; then they retract: they guarantee to him what he paid; similarly for loan (ariyah).
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings (matn) from the Hanafi school on the consequences when witnesses retract their testimony after a judgment has been passed. The key principle is that liability (daman) is based on the portion of the right that is lost due to the retraction; the consideration is for the witnesses who remain, not for those who retract. The text then provides specific applications in various contracts: hire (ijara), mudaraba (profit-sharing partnership), shirka (partnership), shuf'a (pre-emption), inheritance (mirath), bequest (wasiyya), and deposit/loan (wadi'a/ariya). In each case, the ruling depends on whether the retraction caused a loss to the litigants and who bears the guarantee. For example, in the hire case, if both witnesses retract and the animal perished, they guarantee its value minus the hire already paid. In mudaraba, if the profit was not yet distributed, retraction by witnesses does not impose liability. In partnership, if profits were divided before the retraction, the witnesses guarantee the difference between the claimed and admitted share. In pre-emption, if the pre-emptor built on the property, the witnesses guarantee the value of the building if demolition was ordered. In inheritance, if witnesses falsely testified about the father's religion, they guarantee the inheritance to the true heir. In bequest, retraction after judgment makes the witnesses liable for the full amount, unless the retraction occurs after the executor has already consumed the estate. In deposit and loan, the witnesses are liable for what the defendant was forced to pay. These rulings are from the zahir al-riwayah sources like al-Muhit and Kafi al-Hakim.

Key Terms
الرجوع عن الشهادة (al-ruju' 'an al-shahada): A witness retracting his testimony after a judgment has been passed based on it.
الضمان (al-daman): The financial liability or guarantee imposed on the retracting witnesses to compensate for the loss caused.
العبرة لمن بقي (al-'ibra li-man baqiya): The legal consideration is given to the witnesses who remain (do not retract), not to those who retract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of mudaraba (profit-sharing partnership), if two witnesses testify that the mudarib is entitled to half the profit, but the owner admits only one-third, and the witnesses retract after the profit is taken and divided equally, what do the witnesses guarantee?
A) Half the profit
B) One-sixth of the profit
C) Nothing
D) The entire profit

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that retracting witnesses are liable for daman only to the extent of the loss they cause; the testimony of remaining witnesses remains valid.

General Principle of Witness Retraction Liability and the Zakah Analogy
Sharh presents a legal principle and defends it with analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that a retracting witness guarantees half the right, and explain the analogy with zakah that permits a ruling to remain in effect through part of its cause.

Core Idea
A ruling can persist through part of its cause even if not originally established by part, as shown by zakah continuing when part of the nisab remains.

This lesson introduces the foundational principle of witness retraction liability: when one of two witnesses retracts, he guarantees half the right. The commentator addresses an objection that a ruling cannot be established by part of a cause, but he refutes this with a compelling analogy from the zakah obligation. Understanding this principle is essential for calculating liability in more complex multi-witness cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the objection
The text states that if one of two witnesses retracts, he guarantees half, and consideration is given to the remaining witness. An objection is raised: a ruling cannot be established by part of a cause, so it should not remain by part either.
2
Understand the response and analogy
The commentator responds that it is permissible for a ruling to remain by part of a cause even if not originally established by it, drawing an analogy with the lunar year for zakah: the year begins when the nisab is complete, but continues even if part of the nisab is lost.
The key is that continuation is easier than initiation.
3
Apply the principle to a simple case
Apply the rule: if only one witness remains, he establishes half the right, so the retracting witness is liable for the other half.

والعشر نسوة فالسدس على الرجل وخمسة الأسداس على النسوة وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما على الرجل النصف وعلى النسوة النصف لأنهن وإن كثرن يقمن مقام رجل واحد وله أن كل امرأتين مقام رجل واحد للحديث عدلت شهادة كل اثنين منهن بشهادة رجل واحد وإن رجعت العشر فقط فعليهن نصف الحق اتفاقاً كما إذا رجع الرجل وحده، ولو رجع معه ثمان فعليه النصف ولا شيء
قوله : (ضمنوا نصف درهم قال الرملي وجهه كما في تلخيص الجامع أن الحجة تشطرت في درهم إذ ثبت الأول على الثلاثة والرابع على الكل فتأمل قوله : (ضمنوا درهماً ونصفاً الخ) قال الرملي وجهه أنهم اتفقوا جميعاً على الرجوع على الرابع فضمنوه أرباعاً على كل واحد الأول ثابت عليه بالشهادة وحده فتشطرت الحجة فيه فوجب نصفه على الثلاثة أثلاثاً ولا شيء عليه
His statement: (If one of them retracts, he guarantees half, and consideration is for those who remain, not for those who retract) means that half of the right remains established by the testimony of the remaining [witness]. It cannot be said that it is impermissible to establish a ruling by part of a cause, so it should not remain by it either. We say: It is permissible for the ruling to remain by part of a cause even if it was not established by it initially, like the lunar year that begins on the nisab but continues with a part of the nisab even if it did not begin with it. From the cases of al-Jami' al-Kabir: Four [witnesses]? Another retracts, they guarantee half. If a man and two women testify, and a woman retracts, she guarantees one-quarter. If both [women] retract? […] They testify against another for four hundred, and the judge rules accordingly; then one retracts for one hundred, another for that hundred and another hundred, another for the two hundred and another hundred; the retractors owe fifty dirhams in thirds because the testimony stands for three hundred and fifty, since the one who remains testifies for four hundred, and the fourth remains testifying for three hundred, so complete evidence remains for three hundred, no guarantee is required on anyone. For the extra hundred, only one witness remains, so half of the right remains; thus half of it [is lost]. So the retractors are liable because they are equal in causing it. If the fourth retracts from all, they guarantee the hundred in fourths, and additionally they guarantee fifty in thirds besides the first, because there remains [testimony] establishing two hundred and fifty. Thus in al-Muhit. His statement: (If three testify and one retracts, he is not liable) because there remains one who establishes the entire right. His statement: (And if another retracts, they guarantee half) meaning the first and second, because when the first retracted his effect did not appear, but when another retracted, his effect appeared because only enough remains to establish half. In Talkhis al-Jami': If four testify for four dirhams, the judge rules and they are paid, then one retracts for one [dirham], the second for two, the third for three, they guarantee half a dirham, each one-sixth of a dirham, because there remains establishing three and a half. If the fourth retracts from all four, they guarantee one and a half dirhams: on the first one-sixth of the first guaranteed, which is a quarter of a dirham, and on each of the other three a quarter and a sixth of a dirham. His statement: (And if a man and two women testify, and one woman retracts, she guarantees one quarter) because three-quarters of the right remain with the man and one woman. His statement: (And if both [women] retract? they guarantee half) because half the right remains with the man. If two men and two women testify, and a man and a woman retract, they owe one quarter in thirds. If two men retract, they owe half. If two women retract, they owe nothing. His statement: (And if a man and ten women testify, and eight women retract, they are not liable) meaning the eight, because the nisab (minimum number) remains. His statement: (If another woman retracts, she guarantees one quarter) meaning the ninth, because a man and one woman remain. His statement: (If they all retract, the liability is in sixths) meaning the man and the ten women retract: one-sixth on the man and five-sixths on the women. This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], on the man half and on the women half, because however many they are, they stand in the place of one man; and for him [Abu Hanifa] every two women stand in the place of one man, based on the hadith: 'The testimony of every two of them is considered the testimony of one man.' If only the ten women retract, they owe half the right by agreement, just as if the man alone retracted. If he retracts along with eight, he owes half and nothing [on the women?]... His statement: (They guarantee half a dirham) al-Ramli said its justification as in Talkhis al-Jami', that the evidence is split in the dirham since the first [witness] established the third and the fourth established the whole, so reflect. His statement: (They guarantee one and a half dirhams) al-Ramli said its justification that they all agreed to retract against the fourth, so they make him liable in fourths, on each one the first is established by his testimony alone, so the evidence is split in it, so half of it is owed by the three in thirds, and nothing on him.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This is the commentary (sharh) from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding retraction of witnesses. The commentator begins by explaining the general principle: when one witness retracts, he guarantees half of the right because the remaining witness establishes half. He addresses an objection about the validity of a ruling standing by part of its cause, drawing an analogy with zakah: the obligation of zakah begins on a full nisab but can continue even if part of the nisab is lost. Then he provides detailed examples from al-Jami' al-Kabir and Talkhis al-Jami' to illustrate how liability is calculated when multiple witnesses retract in different proportions. For instance, with four witnesses testifying to 400 dirhams, if they retract in various combinations, the calculation follows the principle that the remaining testimony establishes a partial right. The commentator also explains cases involving male and female witnesses: a woman retracting guarantees a quarter if a man remains, and with ten women, the liability is divided in sixths. Importantly, he records a disagreement (ikhtilaf) between Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the proportion when a man and ten women all retract: Abu Hanifa says one-sixth on the man and five-sixths on the women, while the Sahibayn say half and half, because many women stand in place of one man. The commentary concludes with further technical notes from al-Ramli on the justification of the calculations in Talkhis al-Jami'. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of detailed juridical reasoning (ta'lil) and the use of hypothetical cases to derive proportional liability rules.

Key Terms
الحجة (al-hujjah): The evidence or proof provided by witnesses; in this context, the weight of testimony that establishes a right.
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum number of witnesses required for valid testimony; typically two males or one male and two females.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Half the right
C) One quarter
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
A retracting witness guarantees half the right because the remaining witness establishes only half; this is justified by the principle that a ruling can remain by part of its cause.

Liability of Retracting Witnesses: Proof Thresholds and Apportionment
Explains liability for retracting witnesses in multi-witness scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the liability of retracting witnesses in multi-witness cases by applying the Hanafi rule of proof thresholds and the valuation of women's testimony.

Core Idea
Liability equals the fraction of proof lost by retraction, based on each witness's contribution to the niṣāb.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq explains the detailed rules for witness retraction liability. The core principle is that a retracting witness compensates for the portion of proof that is lost, calculated by comparing the remaining witnesses against the required threshold (niṣāb) for a complete proof. Understanding this requires familiarity with the Hanafi valuation of women's testimony as half that of a man and the intra-madhhab disagreement on how to group female witnesses for liability allocation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the witness set and niṣāb threshold
Determine the complete set of witnesses and the standard niṣāb for the case (usually one man or two women for financial claims). Convert all witnesses into male equivalents: a man = 1, two women = 1.
For a man and two women, the total male equivalents = 1 + (2×0.5) = 2. For a man and ten women, total = 1 + (10×0.5) = 6.
2
Analyze each retraction's effect on proof completeness
Check whether the remaining witnesses still constitute a complete proof (≥1 male equivalent). If yes, those who retract owe nothing for that retraction because no proof is lost.
In the man and ten women case, eight women retract leaving man + 2 women = 2 male equivalents ≥1 → no liability for the eight.
3
Calculate the fraction of proof lost
The retracting witness is liable for the fraction by which the proof decreases. Compute the lost portion as a fraction of the original proof (or of the value of the claim), then divide among retractors proportionally.
When one woman retracts from man+2women, remaining = 1.5 male eq. out of 2 → lost 0.5/2 = 1/4 → she pays 1/4.
4
Allocate among multiple retractors
If several retract simultaneously, the total lost proof is split equally among them (each retractor pays an equal share of the lost fraction) unless the ikhtilaf specifies otherwise.
When both women retract from man+2women, lost half of the proof → they jointly pay half, each paying half of that half (1/4 each? Wait, the text says they guarantee the half jointly, meaning each pays half of the half? Actually, the text says 'ضمنتا النصف' implying they jointly guarantee half; typically each pays 1/4 of the claim value. But the sharh clarifies it's per the lost proof fraction.)
5
Apply the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf for total retraction of man and ten women
When all retract, Abu Hanifa counts each two women as one male unit → man is 1 of 6 units → pays 1/6; women 5/6. The Sahibayn treat all women collectively as one male unit → man and women equal 2 units → each party pays 1/2.
The muftā bihi in later practice is often the Sahibayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن شهد رجل وامرأتان فرجعت امرأة ضمنت الربع وإن رجعا ضمنتا النصف وإن شهد رجل وعشر نسوة فرجعت ثمان لم يضمن فإن رجعت أخرى ضمن ربعه فإن رجعوا فالغرم بالأسداس أي رجع الرجل والعشر نسوة فالسدس على الرجل وخمسة الأسداس على النسوة وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما على الرجل النصف وعلى النسوة النصف
And if a man and two women testify, then one woman retracts, she guarantees the quarter; and if both retract, they guarantee the half. And if a man and ten women testify, and eight retract, they guarantee nothing; then if another retracts, she guarantees a quarter of it; then if all retract, the liability is by sixths: that is, when the man and the ten women retract, the man pays one sixth and the women five sixths according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the man pays half and the women pay half.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq lays out the rules for the liability (damān) of witnesses who retract their testimony after a judgment has been executed. The key principle is that the remaining witnesses' testimony must still constitute a complete proof (ḥujja). In the case of a man and two women, the testimony of one man and one woman equals half a proof (since a woman's testimony is half of a man's). Thus, if one woman retracts, one man and one woman remain, which is three-fourths of a full proof, so the retracting woman pays one-quarter. If both women retract, only the man remains, which is half a proof, so they pay half jointly. For a man and ten women, the women collectively count as five men (each two women equal one man). If eight women retract, the remaining two women (equal to one man) plus the man equal two men, a full proof, so no liability. If nine retract, only the man and one woman remain (one and a half men), which is three-fourths, so the ninth woman pays one-quarter. If all retract, the allocation differs between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Abu Hanifa views each two women as one man, so the man is one male witness and ten women are five male equivalents, total six units; the man pays one-sixth, women five-sixths. The Sahibayn consider all women collectively as equivalent to one man (based on the hadith that the testimony of two women equals that of one man), so the man is one and the women collectively one, total two units; the man pays half, women half. This intra-Hanafi difference stems from whether the women's numbers are considered individually (Imam) or as a collective unit (Sahibayn).

Key Terms
الرجوع عن الشهادة (al-rujū' 'an al-shahādah): The act of a witness withdrawing his or her testimony after it has been given and a judgment has been executed.
الضمان (al-ḍamān): Financial compensation required from retracting witnesses for the loss caused by their testimony.
النصاب (al-niṣāb): The required number of witnesses to establish a complete proof in court; for financial claims, it is one man or two women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man and ten women testify for a claim. Nine women retract. According to the passage, what is the liability of the ninth woman?
A) She pays one-sixth of the claim.
B) She pays one-quarter of the claim.
C) She pays one-half of the claim.
D) She pays nothing.

Key Takeaway
The liability of a retracting witness is proportional to the fraction of proof lost, with the niṣāb threshold determining whether any loss occurs.

Liability of Retracting Witnesses in Marriage
Ruling on liability when witnesses retract marriage testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for liability when witnesses retract testimony about a marriage dower, and apply it to cases of proper, excessive, and deficient dower.

Core Idea
Retracting witnesses are not liable if they testified to a proper dower; they only guarantee any excess.

In Hanafi law, when witnesses retract testimony that formed the basis of a marriage contract, their liability depends on whether the dower they testified to matches the proper dower (mahr mithl). This lesson unpacks the principle of 'destruction with exchange' (al-itlāf bi-‘iwaḍ) and its application to marriage testimony, drawing from the matn of Kanz al-Daqā’iq and its commentary in Al-Bahr al-Rā’iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the testimonial scenario
First, recognize the legal situation: two male witnesses testify about a marriage contract, specifying a dower amount. They later retract their testimony.
The scenario is post-marriage; the husband may have paid the dower based on their word.
2
Determine if the dower equals mahr mithl
Check whether the dower they testified to is the proper dower (mahr mithl) for the woman. If it equals mahr mithl, the testimony merely confirms what the law would prescribe anyway.
Mahr mithl is the customary dower for a woman of her status.
3
Apply the principle of al-itlāf bi-‘iwaḍ
If the dower is proper, the retraction does not impose liability because the testimony caused a lawful exchange (the marriage contract with proper dower). Destruction with a compensating exchange is not considered compensable (ka-lā itlāf).
This principle prevents double recovery: the husband gets the marriage, the wife gets the proper dower.
4
Handle the case of an excessive dower
If the witnesses testified to a dower higher than mahr mithl, then upon retraction they are liable for the excess amount. The excess is without exchange (bila ‘iwaḍ), so it is a compensable loss to the husband.
The husband paid more than required; the witnesses caused that loss.
5
Note the case of a deficient dower
The author is silent on testifying to a dower less than mahr mithl. This implies no liability for the deficiency because the marriage is still valid and the wife automatically gets mahr mithl by law; the testimony did not cause a net loss to the husband.
The husband may have paid less, but legally must pay mahr mithl anyway, so no harm from retraction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن شهد رجلان عليه أو عليها بنكاح بقدر مهر مثلها ورجعا لم يضمنا لأنهما أتلفا شيئاً بعوض يقابله والإتلاف بعوض كلا إتلاف قوله : (وإن زاد عليه) (ضمناها أي الزيادة للزوج لأنهما أتلفاها بلا عوض. وسكت المؤلف عما إذا شهدا بأصل النكاح بأقل من مهر مثلها للإشارة إلى أنهما لا يضمنان ما نقص
And if two men testify against him or on his behalf regarding a marriage for a dower equal to her dower mithl, and then they retract, they are not liable because they caused destruction with a corresponding exchange, and destruction with exchange is like no destruction. His saying: (And if they increased [the dower]) they guarantee it, i.e., the increase, to the husband because they caused destruction without exchange. The author remained silent on the case when they testify to the marriage itself for less than her dower mithl, indicating that they do not guarantee the deficiency.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage discusses retraction of testimony in marriage cases. If two witnesses testify that a man married a woman with a proper dower (mahr mithl), and then retract, they are not liable for the dower amount because the testimony caused a valid marriage contract that includes an exchange (the dower). In Hanafi law, destruction with compensation (i.e., the dower received by the wife) is not considered destructive. However, if the witnesses testified that the dower was higher than the proper dower, they are liable for the excess because that excess was not part of the lawful exchange; it was an unjust loss to the husband. The author (in Kanz al-Daqā’iq) did not mention the case where witnesses testify to a marriage with a dower less than the proper dower, implying that they are not liable for the deficiency, because the marriage is still valid and the wife is entitled to the proper dower by law, so the testimony did not cause a loss.

Key Terms
مهر مثلها (mahr mithlihā): The dower appropriate for a woman of her status (family, age, etc.) as determined by custom.
الإتلاف بعوض (al-itlāf bi-‘iwaḍ): Destruction of property that is compensated by a lawful exchange, which is not considered a compensable wrong.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two witnesses testify that a man married a woman for a dower of 5000, which is the proper mahr. They retract. What is the ruling?
A) They must pay 5000 to the husband.
B) They must pay 2500 each.
C) They are not liable for anything.
D) They must pay half the dower.

Key Takeaway
In marriage testimony, retracting witnesses are not liable if the dower equals mahr mithl; only any excess is compensable.

Liability When Mixed Gender Witnesses Retract: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining liability divisions when men and women witnesses retract testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on liability division when mixed-gender witnesses retract, apply the fractions to given scenarios, and evaluate the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa treats each woman as half a man; the Sahibayn treat all women collectively as one man.

When witnesses retract after a judgment, they must compensate the loss. But how is the liability divided when the witnesses are a mix of men and women, whose testimony carries different weight? Within the Hanafi school, there is a key dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents the differing views, corrects an error in al-Muhit, and explores several hypothetical scenarios to illustrate the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
What is the act? Witnesses retracting after a judgment based on their testimony. The consequence is liability (daman). How to divide this liability among multiple retracting witnesses of mixed genders?
The liability is for the loss caused by the false testimony.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Each woman is treated as half a man in mixed company. So the total 'testimonial units' = number of men + (number of women)/2. Liability is divided proportionally per unit.
Example: 1 man + 3 women = 1 + 1.5 = 2.5 units. Man gets 1/2.5 = 2/5 of the total liability.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
All women collectively are equivalent to one man, regardless of number. So the liability is split equally between the men's side and the women's side (half each).
Example: 1 man + 3 women: man gets half, women collectively get half.
4
Apply to specific scenarios
Work through the cases given: 1 man + 10 women, 1 man + 3 women, 2 men + 1 woman, etc. For each, compute the shares per view.
Pay special attention to scenarios where not all witnesses retract.
5
Understand the correction of al-Muhit and thamarah al-khilaf
The author declares al-Muhit's ruling a mistake. The correct views are given. Then note the practical difference: e.g., in 1 man + 3 women, if man and one woman retract, Sahibayn say man pays entire half, Abu Hanifa says they share.
Later works often prefer the Sahibayn's position.
